Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
7 min
Conditions for Salam in Countable Items: Mutaqarib vs. Mutafawit
Hanafi conditions for salam in countable items, with special cases and role of custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mutaqarib (close) and mutafawit (distant) countable items, apply the Hanafi conditions for valid salam in each, and incorporate the role of custom ('urf).

Core Idea
Salam in countable items is valid if variation is negligible; otherwise, additional specifications are needed.

This portion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the criteria for valid salam in countable items. The key distinction is between 'mutaqarib' (items with negligible unit variation, like eggs) and 'mutafawit' (items with significant variation, like watermelons). For mutaqarib, salam is valid by count or measure; for mutafawit, it requires extra specifications like size or weight. The text also addresses unique cases like fals (copper coins) and bricks, where custom determines whether items are treated as price or commodity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of countable items
Understand the definitions: mutaqarib (close, similar) vs. mutafawit (distant, variable). Mutaqarib items can be sold by count; mutafawit require additional specifications.
Examples: eggs (mutaqarib), watermelons (mutafawit).
2
Apply the rule to mutaqarib items
Salam in mutaqarib items is valid by count or by measure (kiilan), per majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). Zufar disagreed on measure but his view is not followed.
The text says: 'wa innama jaza kiilan li wujud al-dabt' (it is only permissible by measure because precision exists).
3
Apply the rule to mutafawit items
Salam in mutafawit items by count alone is invalid. Additional specifications (like length, thickness, weight) are required to eliminate gharar.
The passage lists many examples: watermelon, pumpkin, pomegranate, heads, trotters, pearls, etc.
4
Examine special cases: fals, bricks, and eggs
Fals (copper coin) is treated as thaman while circulating; salam by count is valid if not thaman. Bricks require specification of place of manufacture and delivery. Ostrich eggs and coconuts have differing rulings based on custom.
The text discusses custom ('urf) extensively; e.g., in Egypt, ostrich eggs are purchased for their shells, so they become mutafawit.
5
Understand the role of custom in determining mutaqarib vs. mutafawit
The distinction is not purely inherent to the item but depends on how people customarily treat it. If variation is acceptable in a particular market, it can be mutaqarib.
The passage uses the example of eggplant: allowed in some regions but not in others.

كتاب البيع/ باب السلم في موزون. وقيد المثمن احترازاً عن الدراهم والدنانير فإنه وإن كانت موزونة لكنها ثمن فلا يجوز الإسلام فيها لأن السلم تعجيل الثمن وتأجيل المبيع، ولو جاز فيها انعكس فإذا لم يقع سلماً يكون باطلاً عند عيسى بن أبان. وقال الأعمش بكون بيعاً بثمن مؤجل اعتباراً للمعنى والأول أصح لأنه لا يمكن تصحيحه في غير ما أوجبا العقد فيه. ورجح قول الأعمش في فتح القدير بأنه أدخل في الفقه، وهذا الخلاف فيما إذا أسلم فيهما غير الأثمان كالحنطة، وأما إذا أسلم فيهما الأثمان لم يجز إجماعاً ولو أسلم في المكيل وزناً كما إذا أسلم في البر والشعير بالميزان فيه روايتان والمعتمد الجواز لوجود الضبط وعلى هذا الخلاف لو أسلم في الموزون كيلاً.
قوله: (ويصح في العددي المتقارب كالبيض والجوز لأنه معلوم مضبوط مقدور التسليم وما فيه من التفاوت مهدر عرفاً ولا خلاف في جوازه عدداً إنما الخلاف فيه كيلاً، فعندنا يجوز كيلاً ومنعه زفر كيلاً وعنه منعه والقرع والرمان والرؤوس والأكارع والسفرجل والدر والجواهر واللآليء والأدم والجلود والخشب فلا يجوز السلم في شيء منها عدداً للتفاوت إلا إذا ذكر ضابطاً غير مجرد العدد كطول أو غلظ أو غير ذلك. ومن المتفاوت الجوالق والفاء فلا يجوز إلا بذكر مميزات وأجازوه في الباذنجان إلا بالتزام أن الأعمش قائل بانعقاد البيع بلفظ السلم وإلا فيجوز أن يكون قائلاً بمقابل الأصح من أنه لا يجوز وحينئذ فلا يتم المطلوب. واعترضه أيضاً بأن صاحب الثوب وإن أعطاه له بدراهم مؤجلة لكن على أنها مبيعة لا على أنها ثمن ليلزم أن يكون من أفراد البيع وذكر باقي شروط السلم قرينة على إرادة هذا المعنى فتأمل اهـ وأنت خبير بأن كلاً من الاعتراضين ساقط ؛ أما الأول فلأن فرض المسألة أنه أسلم ثوباً مثلاً في دراهم وقد قال أبو بكر الأعمش : إنه ينعقد بيعاً لا سلماً. فهذا صريح بأنه يقول إن البيع ينعقد بلفظ السلم. وقد ذكر في النهر قبل هذا أن صاحب القنية لم يحك خلافاً في انعقاده بلفظ السلم. وأما الثاني فلأن صاحب الفتح معترف بأن العقد عقد سلم ولكنه اختل بعض شروطه على أنه سلم ووجد اللفظ الذي ينعقد به البيع فيصير العقد عقد بيع لأن كلاً من السلم والبيع يشتركان في كونهما مبادلة مال بمال وقد قصده المتعاقدان ولا مانع شرعاً من كون هذه المبادلة المقصودة إذا لم تصح على صفة خاصة قصدها المتعاقدان أن تصح على صفة أخرى كما إذا قصدا عقد الشركة على صفة كونها مفاوضة وفقد بعض شروطها فإنها تصير شركة عنان وإن لم يقصدا هذه الصفة، ولذلك نظائر كثيرة كما لو وهب للفقير أو تصدق على غني يكون الأول صدقة والثاني هبة وكما لو أقام غيره وصياً في حياته أو وكيلاً بعد وفاته يكون الأول وكيلاً والثاني وصياً، وكما لو اشترى أمة تعدل ألف درهم مع طوق فضة قيمته ألف درهم ونقد من الثمن ألفاً فهو ثمن الفضة، سواء سكت أو قال خذ هذا من ثمنها تحرياً للجواز كما سيأتي في الصرف، ولا يخفى أن تحري الجواز في مسألتنا بالأولى لأنه لم يصرح فيها بخلاف الجائز، وإن صرح فهي مثل مسألة الصرف فتأمل منصفاً.
قوله : (وشرط في الخلاصة ذكر المكان الخ أقول : عبارة الخلاصة هكذا: ولا بأس بالسلم في اللبن والآجر إذا بين الملبن والمكان وذكر عدداً معلوماً والمكان. قال بعضهم: مكان الإيفاء هذا قول أبي حنيفة . وقال بعضهم المكان الذي يضرب فيه اللبن انتهت فكان ينبغي يذكر قول الإمام ولا سيما مع احتمال أن يكون ذلك البعض من غير أهل المذهب.
قوله: (والملبن والكاغد عدداً لإهدار التفاوت. وفي فتح القدير : وفيه نظر ظاهر أو بحمل على كاغد بقالب خاص وإلا فلا يجوز وكون الباذنجان مهدر التفاوت لعله في باذنجان ديارهم وفي ديارنا ليس كذلك بخلاف بيض النعام وجوز الهند لا يستحق شيء منه بالإسلام بخلاف بيض الدجاج والجوز الشامي والفرنجي لعدم إهدار التفاوت. ويشترط مع العدد بيان الصفة أيضاً في شرح الشافي فلو أسلم في بيض النعام أو في جوز الهند جاز كما جاز في الأخيرين، وعن أبي حنيفة أنه عدداً منعه في بيض النعام ادعاء للتفاوت في المالية وهو خلاف ظاهر الرواية. والوجه أن ينظر إلى الغرض في عرف الناس ؛ فإن كان الغرض في ذلك العرف حصول القشر ليتخذ في سلاسل القناديل كما في ديار مصر وغيرها من الأمصار يجب أن نقاء يعمل بهذه الرواية فلا يجوز السلم فيها بعد ذكر العدد إلا مع تعيين المقدار واللون من البياض أو إهداره اهـ . وفي المعراج والفاصل بين المتفاوت والمتقارب أن ما ضمن مستهلكه بالمثل فهو متقارب وبالقيمة يكون متفاوتاً. وفي البزازية : يجوز السلم في الأواني المتخذة . الخزف عدداً إن نوعاً يصير معلوماً عند الناس، ويجوز في الكيزان الخزفية إذا بين نوع لا يتفاوت آحاده اهـ. ولم يشترط المؤلف للجواز إعلام الصفة أنه جيد أو وسط أو رديء ومنهم من شرط أعلام الصفة؛ كذا في الذخيرة وفيها عن أبي يوسف : لو أسلم بيض الأوز في بيض الدجاج أو أسلم بيض النعام في بيض الدجاج جاز، وإن أسلم بيض الدجاج في بيض نعامة أو أسلم بيض الدجاج في بيض الأوز ؛ وإن كان في حين يقدر عليه جاز، فإن كان في حين لا يقدر عليه لا يجوز اهـ .
من قوله : (والفلس) لأنه عددي يمكن ضبطه فيصح السلم فيه ، وقيل لا يصح عند محمد العد لأنه ثمن ما دام يروج وظاهر الرواية عن الكل الجواز. وإذا بطلت ثمنيتها لا يخرج عن إلى الوزن للعرف إلا أن يهدره أهل العرف كما هو في زماننا فإن الفلوس أثمان في زماننا ولا تقبل إلا وزناً فلا يجوز السلم فيها إلا وزناً في ديارنا في زماننا، وقد كانت قبل هذه الأعصار عددية في ديارنا أيضاً؛ كذا في فتح القدير قوله : ((واللبن) بكسر الباء وهو الطوب . ولا بأس بالسلم في اللبن والآجر إذا بين الملبن والمكان وذكر عدداً معلوماً والمكان.
Book of Sales/Chapter of Salam. In weighed items. And the restriction of the price (al-muthaman) is to exclude dirhams and dinars, for although they are weighed, they are price (thaman), so salam in them is not permissible because salam is advancing the price and deferring the sold item. If it were permissible in them, it would be reversed. So if it does not occur as salam, it is void according to 'Isa ibn Aban. And al-A'mash said it becomes a sale with deferred price, considering the meaning. And the first is more correct because it cannot be validated in other than what the contract parties intended. And in Fath al-Qadir, al-A'mash's view is preferred as more jurisprudential. This dispute is when salam is done in them (dirhams/dinars) as non-price items like wheat. But if one does salam in them as price items, it is not permissible by consensus. And if one does salam in measured items by weight, like salam in wheat and barley by weight, there are two narrations, and the relied-upon is permissibility due to the existence of precision. And similarly, if one does salam in weighed items by measure.
He said: (And it is valid in close countable items like eggs and walnuts) because they are known, precise, and capable of delivery, and any variation is disregarded customarily. There is no dispute about its permissibility by count; the dispute is by measure. According to us, it is permissible by measure, but Zufar prohibits it by measure. And from him also a prohibition by count due to variation, and we answered him. It is only permissible by measure because precision exists. And the restriction to closeness includes pears, apricots, and figs, as in the furuq of al-Karabisi, because distant countable items are not permissible in salam. And what has varied in its value, like watermelon, pumpkin, pomegranate, heads, trotters, quince, pearls, jewels, gems, leather, skins, and wood, salam in any of them by count is not permissible due to variation, unless a specification other than mere count is mentioned, like length or thickness or other. Among the distant items are sacks and ... so it is not permissible unless with distinguishing features. And they permitted it in eggplant only by accepting that al-A'mash holds the contract of sale with the word salam; otherwise it may be that he holds the opposite of the correct view that it is not permissible, and then the desired result is not achieved. And he also objected that the owner of the cloth, although he gave it to him for deferred dirhams, but on the basis that they are sold, not that they are price, so it would be an instance of sale, and mentioning the remaining conditions of salam is a presumption for intending this meaning, so reflect. And you are aware that both objections are invalid. As for the first, because the premise of the issue is that he did salam in a cloth, for example, for dirhams, and Abu Bakr al-A'mash said that it becomes a sale, not a salam. This is explicit that he says the sale is concluded with the word salam. And it was mentioned in al-Nahr before this that the author of al-Qunyah did not relate a dispute about its conclusion with the word salam. As for the second, because the author of Fath acknowledges that the contract is a salam contract but some of its conditions as salam were missing, and the word that concludes a sale is found, so the contract becomes a sale contract, because both salam and sale share in being an exchange of property for property, and the two parties intended it, and there is no legal impediment to this intended exchange, if it does not validate as a specific form intended by the parties, that it validates as another form, like if they intended a partnership contract as a muwafadah and some of its conditions are missing, it becomes an 'inan partnership even if they did not intend this form. And there are many analogies to that, like if one gifts to a poor person or gives charity to a rich person, the first is charity and the second is a gift, and like if one appoints another as executor during his life or as agent after his death, the first is an agent and the second is an executor, and like if one buys a slave girl valued at a thousand dirhams with a silver necklace valued at a thousand dirhams and pays a thousand dirhams as the price, it is the price of the silver, whether he remains silent or says 'take this from its price', seeking validity as will come in currency exchange. And it is not hidden that seeking validity in our issue is even more so, because he did not explicitly state anything contrary to the valid, and if he did, it is like the currency exchange issue, so reflect fairly.
He said: (And the condition in al-Khulasa is to mention the place, etc.) I say: The expression of al-Khulasa is as follows: There is no harm in salam in bricks and baked bricks if the place of making bricks and the location are specified, and a known number and the place are mentioned. Some said: The place of delivery is the saying of Abu Hanifa. And some said the place where the bricks are made. End. So he should have mentioned the Imam's saying, especially since that someone may be from outside the school.
He said: (And the brick and paper by count due to disregard of variation. And in Fath al-Qadir: There is apparent doubt in it, or it is interpreted as paper with a specific mold, otherwise it is not permissible. And that eggplant has disregarded variation is perhaps in their region, but in our region it is not so, unlike ostrich eggs and coconuts, nothing is entitled from them by salam, unlike chicken eggs and Syrian and Frankish walnuts, due to lack of disregard of variation. And it is required along with count to mention the quality also, as in Sharh al-Shafi. So if one does salam in ostrich eggs or coconuts, it is permissible as it is permissible in the latter two. And from Abu Hanifa that by count he prohibited it in ostrich eggs claiming variation in value, which is contrary to the zahir al-riwaya. And the correct approach is to consider the customary purpose; if the purpose in that custom is to obtain the shell to make into lamp chains, as in Egypt and other regions, then it is necessary to act on this narration, so salam in them is not permissible after mentioning the count unless specifying the quantity and color of whiteness or disregard. End. And in al-Mi'raj: The distinction between distant and close is that what is guaranteed by its equivalent in case of destruction is close, and by value is distant. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: Salam is permissible in utensils made of pottery by count if the type becomes known to people, and it is permissible in pottery mugs if the type is specified such that individual pieces do not vary. End. And the author did not require for validity the indication of quality (good, medium, or poor), and some required indication of quality; as in al-Dhakhira, and in it from Abu Yusuf: If one does salam in goose eggs for chicken eggs, or does salam in ostrich eggs for chicken eggs, it is permissible. And if one does salam in chicken eggs for ostrich eggs, or does salam in chicken eggs for goose eggs, if at a time when they are available, it is permissible; if at a time when they are not available, it is not permissible. End.
From his saying: (And the fals) because it is countable and can be precisely specified, so salam in it is valid. And it is said it is not valid according to Muhammad due to it being a price as long as it circulates. And the apparent narration from all is permissibility. And if its price-ness ceases, it does not exit to weight unless the custom treats it as such, except if custom disregards it as is in our time, for fals are prices in our time and are only accepted by weight, so salam in them is not permissible except by weight in our region in our time, and before these times they were countable in our region as well. As in Fath al-Qadir. His saying: (And al-labn) with kasra on the ba, meaning bricks. And there is no harm in salam in bricks and baked bricks if the place of making bricks and the location are specified, and a known number and the place are mentioned.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a detailed commentary on the chapter of salam from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses two main issues: the validity of salam in dirhams and dinars, and the permissibility of salam in countable items. The text begins by stating that salam in dirhams and dinars is invalid because they are typically used as prices (thaman) not as goods (muthaman). There is a key intra-Hanafi dispute: 'Isa ibn Aban holds such a contract void if conditions of salam are unmet, while al-A'mash argues it becomes a valid sale with deferred price. The commentator notes that in Fath al-Qadir, al-A'mash's view is preferred but that the majority follow the first opinion. He then discusses an objection about a cloth exchanged for deferred dirhams, and provides a detailed refutation using analogies from partnership, gifts, and agency to show that contracts can transform when conditions fail, provided the exchange nature is preserved. The second major section deals with countable items. Items that are 'muttaqarib' (similar in units) like eggs and walnuts are valid for salam by count or measure, as variation is negligible. Items that are 'mutafawit' (dissimilar) like watermelons or precious stones are not valid by count alone unless additional specifications (size, weight, color) are given. The text then addresses specific items: eggplant, paper, bricks, and fals (copper coins). For fals, the ruling depends on custom: if they circulate as prices, salam in them is invalid by count but may be valid by weight. For bricks, the place of manufacture and delivery must be specified according to Abu Hanifa. Throughout, the commentator cites multiple sources (al-Karabisi, Fath al-Qadir, al-Bazzaziyya, al-Dhakhira, etc.) and presents differences among Hanafi scholars, including Zufar, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. The final part emphasizes that custom ('urf) plays a crucial role in determining whether variation is disregarded.

Key Terms
عددي متقارب (adadi mutaqarib): Items that are counted and whose individual units are similar enough that variation is negligible in custom.
متفاوت (mutafawit): Items that vary significantly in value individually, requiring more than mere count to specify.
ضابط (dabit): A specification that controls variability, such as length, thickness, or weight.
عرف (urf): Customary practice that influences the legal classification of items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is salam in 50 watermelons by count alone valid?
A) Yes, because watermelons are countable.
B) No, because watermelons are mutafawit and require additional specifications.
C) Yes, if the watermelons are all similar in size.
D) No, because salam in fresh produce is never allowed.

Key Takeaway
Salam in countable items is valid only if the items are mutaqarib or additional specifications are provided for mutafawit items; custom plays a key role in classification.

The Criterion of Uniform vs. Disparate in Salam
Explaining salam conditions for eggs, coconuts, and paper.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion (liability by like vs. value) to distinguish uniform from disparate items and determine the validity of salam by count for items like paper and ostrich eggs.

Core Idea
Salam by count is valid only if items are uniform in value; if disparate, count alone is insufficient.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the critical distinction between uniform (mutaqārib) and disparate (mutafāwit) items in salam contracts. The Hanafi school relies on this distinction to determine when a salam contract can be concluded simply by specifying the number and type, and when additional description of quality is required. The commentator expands on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, addressing paper, eggs, and even local customs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
We are examining the validity of salam (forward sale) for items that are naturally somewhat variable in size and quality, such as eggs, coconuts, paper. The core question: can salam be validly concluded by merely specifying the count and type?
2
Define the two categories
The passage from al-Mi'raj gives the criterion: an item is uniform (mutaqārib) if the consumer's liability in case of destruction is by the like (mithl); it is disparate (mutafāwit) if liability is by value (qīmah). Apply this to eggs: chicken eggs are generally uniform; ostrich eggs are more variable.
Criterion: الضمان بالمثل مقابل الضمان بالقيمة
3
Apply to paper and eggplant
Paper is considered uniform by custom (disparity is negligible). Eggplant disparity depends on local custom (in some lands it might be uniform). This shows the role of 'urf.
Custom can make a disparate item uniform in a given locale.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on ostrich eggs
Although some narrations from Abu Hanifa prohibit salam in ostrich eggs by count, the relied-upon (zahir al-riwayah) position allows it with description. The commentator advises looking at the actual purpose (e.g., if buying for the shell, need to specify color and size).
The dispute is within the Hanafi school; the tarjih is permissibility with description.
5
Derive the rule
Valid salam by count requires the item to be uniform according to custom; if disputed, additional specification (quality, size) may be needed. The mufta bihi is that salam in items with negligible disparity is valid with count and description, subject to custom.

والكاغد عدداً لإهدار التفاوت. وفي فتح القدير : وفيه نظر ظاهر أو بحمل على كاغد بقالب خاص وإلا فلا يجوز وكون الباذنجان مهدر التفاوت لعله في باذنجان ديارهم وفي ديارنا ليس كذلك بخلاف بيض النعام وجوز الهند لا يستحق شيء منه بالإسلام بخلاف بيض الدجاج والجوز الشامي والفرنجي لعدم إهدار التفاوت. ويشترط مع العدد بيان الصفة أيضاً في شرح الشافي فلو أسلم في بيض النعام أو في جوز الهند جاز كما جاز في الأخيرين، وعن أبي حنيفة أنه عدداً منعه في بيض النعام ادعاء للتفاوت في المالية وهو خلاف ظاهر الرواية. والوجه أن ينظر إلى الغرض في عرف الناس ; فإن كان الغرض في ذلك العرف حصول القشر ليتخذ في سلاسل القناديل كما في ديار مصر وغيرها من الأمصار يجب أن نقاء[؟] يعمل بهذه الرواية فلا يجوز السلم فيها بعد ذكر العدد إلا مع تعيين المقدار واللون من البياض أو إهداره اهـ . وفي المعراج والفاصل بين المتفاوت والمتقارب أن ما ضمن مستهلكه بالمثل فهو متقارب وبالقيمة يكون متفاوتاً. وفي البزازية : يجوز السلم في الأواني المتخذة . الخزف عدداً إن نوعاً يصير معلوماً عند الناس، ويجوز في الكيزان الخزفية إذا بين نوع لا يتفاوت آحاده اهـ. ولم يشترط المؤلف للجواز إعلام الصفة أنه جيد أو وسط أو رديء ومنهم من شرط أعلام الصفة؛ كذا في الذخيرة وفيها عن أبي يوسف : لو أسلم بيض الأوز في بيض الدجاج أو أسلم بيض النعام في بيض الدجاج جاز، وإن أسلم بيض الدجاج في بيض نعامة أو أسلم بيض الدجاج في بيض الأوز ; وإن كان في حين يقدر عليه جاز، فإن كان في حين لا يقدر عليه لا يجوز اهـ .
And paper by count because disparity is negligible. And in Fath al-Qadir: There is apparent consideration in it, or it is restricted to paper of a specific mold, otherwise it is not permissible. And the fact that eggplant has negligible disparity is perhaps in the eggplant of their lands, but in our land it is not like that. Unlike ostrich eggs and coconut, nothing from them is valid by Islam [salam]? Unlike chicken eggs and Syrian and European walnuts due to lack of negligible disparity. And with the number, description of quality is also required in Sharh al-Shafi. So if one makes salam in ostrich eggs or coconut, it is permissible just as it is permissible in the latter two. And from Abu Hanifa: he prohibited it by count in ostrich eggs claiming disparity in value, and that contradicts the apparent narration. The correct view is to look at the purpose in the custom of people: if the purpose in that custom is to obtain the shell to make lamp chains as in Egypt and other cities, then it must be that... one acts by this narration, so salam in them after mentioning the number is not permissible except with specifying the quantity and the color of whiteness or ignoring it. And in al-Mi'raj: the distinction between disparate and uniform is that whatever is guaranteed by the consumer by the like is uniform, and by value is disparate. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: salam is permissible in vessels made of pottery by count if the type is known among people, and it is permissible in pottery jugs if the type is specified such that its individuals do not differ. And the author did not require for validity the declaration of quality—good, medium, or low—and some did require declaration of quality. Likewise in al-Dhakhirah and in it from Abu Yusuf: if one makes salam of goose eggs for chicken eggs or makes salam of ostrich eggs for chicken eggs, it is permissible. And if one makes salam of chicken eggs for ostrich eggs or makes salam of chicken eggs for goose eggs: if it is at a time when it can be obtained, it is permissible; if it is at a time when it cannot be obtained, it is not permissible.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (talil) about salam in items where individual units may have negligible disparity. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq. The key principle: salam is valid in items counted by number only if the disparity in value is negligible (mughaffal). For paper, it is by count because disparity is ignored. Imam Abu Hanifa reportedly prohibited salam in ostrich eggs by count due to disparity, but the relied-upon (zahir al-riwayah) position allows it. The commentator advises looking at custom ('urf): if the purpose is just the shell, then additional specification (quantity, color) is needed. The distinction between uniform and disparate items is based on guarantee: if the consumer's liability is by the like (mithl), the item is uniform; if by value, it is disparate. Abu Yusuf's ruling on cross-salam in eggs depends on availability. The author did not require specification of quality, but some scholars did.

Key Terms
المتفاوت والمتقارب (al-mutafāwit wa al-mutaqārib): Disparate and uniform items: the distinction is that if the consumer's liability is by the like (mithl), it is uniform; if by value, it is disparate.
السلم (al-salam): A forward sale where payment is made in advance for goods to be delivered later.
الغرر (al-gharar): Uncertainty or risk that may invalidate a contract; avoiding gharar is a key principle in salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from al-Mi'raj, what is the criterion to determine if an item is uniform (mutaqārib) or disparate (mutafāwit)?
A) Whether it is sold by weight or by count
B) Whether the consumer's guarantee is by the like (mithl) or by value
C) Whether the item is agricultural or manufactured
D) Whether the Prophet explicitly mentioned it in hadith

Key Takeaway
Salam by count is valid only for items that are uniform in value per custom; otherwise, additional description is needed to avoid gharar.

Cross-Salam in Eggs and the Role of Custom
Explaining salam conditions for eggs, coconuts, and paper.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the permissibility of cross-salam (e.g., chicken eggs for goose eggs) based on availability and custom, applying the ruling of Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Cross-salam in eggs is valid only if the delivered item is available at the time; if not, it is invalid due to potential gharar.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq includes a ruling from Imam Abu Yusuf on cross-salam between different types of eggs. The ruling hinges on the availability of the item at the time of delivery. This lesson explores the interplay of custom ('urf) and practical feasibility in salam contracts, as well as the broader principle that salam items must be present in the market at the delivery date.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
Abu Yusuf considers two scenarios: salam of goose eggs in exchange for chicken eggs, and vice versa. The key variable is which type of egg is being delivered.
2
First scenario: salam of goose eggs for chicken eggs
Valid regardless of season because chicken eggs are usually available year-round. The contract is permissible because the item can be obtained at delivery time.
3
Second scenario: salam of chicken eggs for goose eggs
Valid only if goose eggs are available at the time of delivery; if not, invalid. Availability depends on season and custom.
The phrase 'in yakunu fi hin yuqdiru 'alayhi jaza' indicates conditionality.
4
Extract the principle
The permissibility depends on the ability to obtain the item (al-qudrah 'alayhi) at the time of delivery. This reflects the Hanafi concern with eliminating gharar (uncertainty).
5
Connect to custom
The commentator earlier noted that custom determines whether items are considered uniform. Here, custom also determines availability. The same principle applies to other seasonal items.

Salam in Fulus: The Role of Custom in Counting vs Weighing
Expansion on the ruling of salam in fulus with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on salam in fulus and apply the rule that custom ('urf) determines whether counting or weighing is required.

Core Idea
Custom can override the default ruling: fulus shift from countable to weighable if 'urf changes.

Copper coins (fulus) can be sold in a salam contract either by counting or by weight, depending on how they circulate. The Hanafi school has an internal difference on the default ruling, but the later position—reflected in Fath al-Qadir—holds that the prevailing custom determines the method. This lesson unpacks how custom can transform a legal ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the dispute
The matn mentions 'والفلس'. The commentator expands: Is salam in fulus valid by counting? There is a known ikhtilaf between Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf).
Understand the default ruling: fulus are countable (عددي) so salam by counting is normally valid.
2
Examine the basis of the dispute
Imam Muhammad argues that as long as fulus circulate as a price (ثمن), they must be weighed to avoid riba; therefore counting is invalid. The zahir al-riwayah from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permits counting because fulus are inherently countable.
This is a methodological difference: is the nature of fulus as a price overriding their countability?
3
Analyze the role of custom
The commentator notes that even if fulus lose their status as price, they do not automatically become weighable; custom decides. In the author's time, fulus are still prices but are accepted only by weight, so salam must be by weight.
Custom (العرف) can change the effective ruling even if the default principle remains.
4
Apply to the author's context
In the author's locality and era, fulus are accepted only by weight. Therefore salam in fulus is valid only if the quantity is specified by weight, not by count. The ruling is mufta bihi.
This shows the importance of examining local practice before issuing a fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والفلس) لأنه عددي يمكن ضبطه فيصح السلم فيه ، وقيل لا يصح عند محمد العد لأنه ثمن ما دام يروج وظاهر الرواية عن الكل الجواز. وإذا بطلت ثمنيتها لا يخرج عن إلى الوزن للعرف إلا أن يهدره أهل العرف كما هو في زماننا فإن الفلوس أثمان في زماننا ولا تقبل إلا وزناً فلا يجوز السلم فيها إلا وزناً في ديارنا في زماننا، وقد كانت قبل هذه الأعصار عددية في ديارنا أيضاً؛ كذا في فتح القدير
His saying: (and the fals) because it is countable, can be regulated, so salam in it is valid. And it is said: it is not valid according to Muhammad due to counting because it is a price as long as it circulates, and the apparent narration from all is permissibility. And if its being a price [thaman] becomes invalid, it does not exit from? to weight due to custom, unless the people of custom ignore it as in our time. For the fulus are prices in our time and are not accepted except by weight, so salam in them is not permissible except by weight in our lands in our time, and they were before these eras counted in our lands as well; likewise in Fath al-Qadir
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the matn word 'والفلس' (the fals). The Hanafi school discusses whether fulus (copper coins) can be the subject of salam by counting. According to Imam Muhammad, when fulus circulate as a price (thaman), they are considered like currency and should be sold by weight to avoid riba, so salam by counting is invalid. However, the zahir al-riwayah from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf allows salam by counting because fulus are countable items. The commentator notes that if the fulus lose their status as price (i.e., they are no longer used as currency), they revert to being weighed goods according to custom. In the author's time, fulus were still prices but were accepted only by weight, so salam must be by weight. The lesson shows how custom ('urf) can change the legal ruling.

Key Terms
الفلس (al-fals): A copper coin used as currency; can be counted or weighed depending on custom.
السلم (al-salam): A forward sale where the price is paid upfront and the goods delivered later.
العددي (al-'adadi): Something that is counted, such as coins or eggs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on salam in fulus in the author's time and place?
A) Salam by counting is valid
B) Salam by weight is valid, but counting is also permissible
C) Salam is not valid at all
D) Salam by weight is required; counting is not permissible

Key Takeaway
The validity of salam in fulus depends on local custom: if the custom is to weigh, weight is required; if to count, counting suffices.

Conditions for Salam in Bricks: Mold and Place
Expansion of matn conditions for salam in bricks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two essential specifications for a valid salam in bricks (labin and ajur) and explain the rationale based on need and prevention of dispute.

Core Idea
Salam in bricks requires specifying the mold (milban) and place of manufacture to avoid disputes.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding salam in building materials. It clarifies that for unbaked bricks (labin) and baked bricks (ajur), the contract must specify the mold (milban) and the place of manufacture. The reasoning ties into the Hanafi principle that salam prioritizes uniformity of size due to need, unlike ordinary sale where quality (baking) is paramount. Understanding this distinction is crucial for drafting valid salam contracts in construction commodities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
What conditions must be fulfilled for a salam contract in bricks (labin) and tiles (ajur) to be valid?
The passage focuses on two specific commodities: sun-dried bricks and baked bricks/tiles.
2
Extract the ruling from the matn and commentary
The author quotes the matn 'واللبن والآجر' and then adds conditions: the mold (milban) must be known, and the place of manufacture must be mentioned (from al-Khulasah). Note that if a brick is sold from a mold without specification, it is invalid (from al-Dhakhirah).
The key phrase: 'إن سمى ملبن معلوم' – if he specifies a known mold.
3
Analyze the reasoning (talil)
Why are these conditions necessary? Because bricks are uniform in size when the same mold is used, but they vary in baking. In salam, we prioritize size uniformity (due to need) and disregard baking variation. In sale, baking variation matters. Without specifying the mold and place, the contract leads to dispute (naqf).
The author contrasts salam (forward sale) with ordinary sale: in salam, need justifies overlooking quality differences, so size is key; in sale, quality is key.
4
Identify the consequence of omission
If the mold or place is not specified, the salam contract becomes fasid (invalid) because it leads to uncertainty (gharar) and potential dispute.
The text says: 'إذا لم تعين لا يجوز لإفضائه إلى المنازعة' – if not specified, it is not valid because it leads to dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (واللبن) بكسر الباء وهو الطوب ... وشرط في الخلاصة ذكر المكان الذي يعمل فيه اللبن، وفي الذخيرة: لو باع آجرة من ملبن لم تجز من غير إشارة لأن اللبن من المعاود المتقارب باعتبار قدره ومن المتفاوت باعتبار نضجه فاعتبر الأول في السلم للحاجة واعتبر الثاني في البيع قوله : (والآجر) بضم الجيم وتشديد الراء مع المد أشهر من التخفيف الواحدة آجرة وهو معرب وهو اللين إذا طبخ ; كذا في المصباح قوله : (إن) سمى ملبن معلوم) لأن آحادها لا تتفاوت إذا عينت الآلة وإذا لم تعين لا يجوز لإفضائه إلى المنازعة وفي المصباح : اللبن بكسر الباء ما يعلم من الطين يبنى به الواحدة لبنة ويجوز التخفيف فيصير مثل حمل ..اهـ. والملبن بكسر الباء قالب الطين والمحلب أيضاً ; كذا في الصحاح والمراد الأول
His saying: (and al-labin) with kasra on the ba, and it is the brick... And in al-Khulasah it is stipulated to mention the place where the brick is made. And in al-Dhakhirah: if one sells a tile from a mold (milban) without specification, it is not valid because the brick is uniform in terms of size but disparate in terms of baking. So the first [uniformity] is considered in salam due to need, and the second [disparity] is considered in sale. His saying: (and al-ajur) with damm on the jim and tashdid on the ra with elongation, more famous than lightening, singular ajurah, and it is arabicized; it is the baked clay. Likewise in al-Misbah. His saying: (if) he specifies a known mold (milban) because its individuals do not differ when the tool is specified, and if not specified it is not valid because it leads to dispute. And in al-Misbah: al-labin (with kasr ba) is what is known of clay used for building, singular labinah, and it is permissible to lighten it so it becomes like haml... And al-milban (with kasr ba) is the clay mold, and also al-mihlab; likewise in al-Sihah, and the intended meaning is the first.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the matn words 'واللبن والآجر'. The author explains that for salam in unbaked bricks (labin) and baked bricks (ajur), it is necessary to specify the mold (milban) and the place of manufacture. In al-Khulasah, the place is required. The reason: bricks are uniform in size (if the mold is specified) but disparate in baking; in salam, we prioritize uniformity (size) because need justifies the contract, while in a simple sale we prioritize quality (baking). If the mold is not specified, salam is invalid due to potential dispute. The linguistic notes clarify the terms: labin (brick), ajur (baked brick/tile), milban (mold).

Key Terms
الملبن (al-milban): A mold for making bricks; specifying it ensures uniformity of size in salam.
اللبن (al-labin): Sun-dried brick or adobe; the raw material before baking.
الآجر (al-ajur): Baked brick or tile; the fired version of labin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it necessary to specify the mold (milban) in salam for bricks according to the passage?
A) Because bricks are always sold by weight
B) Because individuals do not differ when the tool is specified
C) Because the Prophet forbade unspecified salam
D) Because bricks are perishable

Key Takeaway
For a valid salam in bricks, the mold (milban) and place of manufacture must be specified to prevent disputes arising from size and baking variations.

Salam in Measured Items (Cloth) and the Prohibition of Salam in Animals
Defining conditions for salam in cloth and ruling out animals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid salam contract in cloth and explain why salam in animals is invalid according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Salam in measured items is valid by consensus due to need, but animals are excluded because their hidden disparity cannot be specified.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the conditions for salam in cloth and similar items measured by length. While salam is originally based on need and not explicitly mentioned in the primary texts, the Hanafi school relies on consensus (ijma) for its validity in mudhru'at. However, the same reasoning does not extend to animals, as their internal variation cannot be adequately specified, leading to prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage clarifies the validity of salam in items measured by length (mudhru'at) and the invalidity of salam in animals.
2
Examine the proof for mudhru'at
The proof is consensus (ijma) and the reason of need (hajah). Note that it is not analogized from weighed/measured items because the need is universal.
The dalil is ijma and the textual indication that salam was legislated for need.
3
Understand the specification requirements for cloth
To avoid dispute, salam in cloth requires specification of length (cubit), type (sifah), and workmanship (san'ah). For silk, weight is also required.
The cubit, if left absolute, defaults to a medium cubit (dhira' wasat).
4
Analyze the cubit dispute
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the meaning of 'medium cubit': some say it refers to the act of measuring (neither too tight nor loose), others to a specific measuring stick. The correct view combines both.
This affects what the buyer receives if the cubit is not defined.
5
Explain the prohibition in animals
Salam in animals is invalid because although the exterior can be regulated, the interior (e.g., health, temperament) cannot, leading to unavoidable dispute.
Borrowing animals is also invalid, but they are guaranteed by value if possessed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والذرعي ) أي ويصح السلم في المذروعات لأنه يمكن ضبطها بما ذكره، وجواز فيها بالإجماع كالثياب والبسط والحصر والبواري. وإنما جاز فيها مع أنها لم تذكر في النص وهو مشروع على خلاف القياس في المكيل والموزون فلا يقاس عليهما للإجماع ودلالة النص لأن سبب شرعيته الحاجة وهي لا تختلف قوله : (كالثوب إذا بين الذراع أي من أي جنس كذا ذكر العيني. وفي فتح القدير : أي قدره كذا كذا ذراعاً. وفي البزازية : إذا أطلق ذكر الذراع في الثوب فله ذراع وسط . وفي الذخيرة: واختلف المشايخ في تفسير قول محمد ذراع وسط; منهم من قال أراد به المصدر وهو فعل الذرع لا لا يعني يمد كل المد ولا يرخى كل الإرخاء، وبعضهم قال أراد به الخشب، والصحيح أنه يحمل عليهما إذا شرط مطلقاً فيكون له الوسط منهما نظراً للجانبين قوله : (والصفة) أي قطن أو كتان أو مركب منهما وهو الملحم أو حرير ونحو ذلك قوله : (والصنعة) أي عمل الشام أو الروم أو زيد أو لأنه معلوماً بذكر هذه الأشياء فلا يؤدي إلى النزاع. ولم يذكر الوزن لأنه ليس بشرط إلا في الحرير إذا بيع وزناً لأنه لا يعلم إلا بالوزن. وفي الظهيرية : ولا يشترط ذكر الوزن في الكرباس واختلفوا في الحرير والصحيح اشتراطه، ولو أسلم في ثوب الخزان بين الطول والعرض والرقعة ولم يذكر الوزن جاز، وإن ذكر الوزن فقط لا يجوز. ولو باع ثوب خز بثوب خز يداً بيد لا يجوز إلا وزناً لأنه لا يباع إلا وزناً اهـ . وفي البزازية : أسلم قطناً هروياً في ثوب هروي جاز وإن مسحا في شعر مسح إن كان المسح عاد شعراً لا يجوز وإلا يجوز ثم قال في نوع : لو أسلم في ثوب وسط وجاء بالجيد فقال خذ هذا وزدني درهما فستأتي مسائله عند قوله ولا يجوز التصرف في المسلم فيه قبل قبضه قوله : (لا) في الحيوان أي لا يصح السلم فيه لتفاوت آحاده لأنه وإن أمكن ضبط ظاهره ولا يمكن ضبط باطنه وكذا استقراضه فاسد ولكنه مضمون بالقيمة مملوك بالقبض
His saying: (and al-dhira'i) i.e., salam is valid in measured items (mudhru'at) because they can be regulated by what he mentioned, and its permissibility is by consensus, like garments, mats, rugs, and reed mats. It is permissible although it is not mentioned in the text, and it is legislated contrary to analogy for weighed and measured items, so it is not analogized to them due to consensus and textual indication, because the reason for its legislation is need, which does not differ. His saying: (like a garment when the cubit is specified) i.e., from any type – thus mentioned al-Ayni. And in Fath al-Qadir: i.e., its length is such-and-such cubits. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: if the mention of the cubit is absolute in a garment, he gets a medium cubit. And in al-Dhakhirah: the mashayikh differed in interpreting the statement of Muhammad 'a medium cubit'; some said he meant the source [masdar] which is the act of cubit-measuring i.e., he neither stretches fully nor relaxes fully; and some said he meant the stick; the correct view is that it applies to both when absolute, so he gets the middle of both considering the two sides. His saying: (and al-sifah) i.e., cotton, linen, or a composite of the two which is mulham, or silk and the like. His saying: (and al-sun'ah) i.e., the workmanship of Sham or Rum or Zayd or 'Amr, because it becomes known by mentioning these things, so it does not lead to dispute. And he did not mention weight because it is not a condition except for silk when sold by weight because it is not known except by weight. And in al-Zahiriyyah: mention of weight is not required in coarse cloth (kirbas), and they differed regarding silk, and the correct view is that it is required. And if one makes salam in a silk garment specifying length, width, and number of patches, without mentioning weight, it is valid; but if he mentions weight only, it is not valid. And if one sells a silk garment for a silk garment hand to hand, it is not valid except by weight because it is only sold by weight. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: if one makes salam of Herati cotton for a Herati garment, it is valid. And if one makes salam of felt for hair felt, if the felt is hair, it is not valid, otherwise it is valid. Then he said: if one makes salam in a medium garment and brings a good one and says 'take this and give me an extra dirham', its issues will come when he says 'it is not permissible to dispose of the subject of salam before taking possession'. His saying: (not) in animals i.e., salam in them is not valid due to the disparity of their individuals, because although its exterior can be regulated, its interior cannot be regulated. Likewise, borrowing them is invalid, but it is guaranteed by value and possessed by taking possession.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the matn words 'والذرعي', 'والصفة', 'والصنعة', and 'لا في الحيوان'. It covers salam in items measured by length (mudhru'at) like cloth, which is valid by consensus despite not being explicitly in the primary texts (Quran/Sunnah). The reason is need (hajah). For cloth, one must specify the length in cubits (dhira'), and if not specified, a medium cubit is used. The type (sifah) must be mentioned (cotton, linen, silk, etc.) and the workmanship (san'ah) (origin or maker). Weight is not required except for silk, which is usually sold by weight. The passage also discusses salam in felt and animal hair garments. Finally, salam in animals is invalid because of hidden disparity; borrowing them is also invalid, but they are guaranteed by value if acquired through possession. This shows the general principle that salam requires precise specification to avoid future dispute.

Key Terms
الذرع (al-dhira'): Measure by cubit; a unit of length. In salam, if absolute, a medium cubit is intended (neither too tight nor too loose).
المذروعات (al-mudhru'at): Items sold by linear measure (cubit), such as cloth, rugs, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is salam in animals invalid according to the passage?
A) Because animals cannot be possessed
B) Because their exterior is uniform but interior is disparate and cannot be checked
C) Because the Prophet explicitly forbade it
D) Because they are measured by weight

Key Takeaway
Salam in measured items like cloth is valid by consensus with precise specifications; salam in animals is invalid due to the impossibility of specifying hidden characteristics.

Conditions for Salam in Bricks and Cubit-Measured Items
Clarifying conditions for salam in bricks and cubit-measured goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific conditions required for a valid salam contract in bricks and cubit-measured items, and explain the consensus proof that permits salam in items measured by length despite being contrary to analogy.

Core Idea
Salam in bricks requires specifying the mold; in cloth, specifying cubit, description, and workmanship – consensus allows it despite being contrary to qiyas.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq (a commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq) clarifies the detailed conditions for salam (advance payment sale) in items measured by cubit (madhru'at) and in bricks. While salam is primarily known for weighed or measured commodities, Hanafi jurists extend it to cubit-measured items by consensus and public need. The text explains why these specifications are essential to avoid dispute and discusses the interpretation of 'middle cubit' among Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of goods
The passage covers bricks (laban and ajar) and cubit-measured items (madhru'at). For each, note the key condition required for validity.
Bricks need mold specification; cubit items need length, description, and workmanship.
2
Analyze the condition for bricks
The text states that the mold (malbin) must be specified because bricks can vary in size and baking. If unspecified, the contract is invalid due to potential dispute. Understand why mold specification suffices (tool standardizes shape).
The passage cites al-Dhakhira and al-Misbah for lexicography.
3
Analyze the conditions for cubit-measured items
Three specifications are required: the cubit (length), the description (cotton, linen, etc.), and the workmanship (origin of labor). Note that weight is generally not required except for silk.
The 'middle cubit' has two interpretations: moderate stretching or a standard stick; the correct view combines both.
4
Examine the proof: consensus and need
Salam in cubit-measured items is permissible by consensus (ijma) even though it is not explicitly in the Quran/Sunnah and is contrary to qiyas on weighed/measured items. The reason is public need, which is the same for all types of goods.
The dalil block shows ijma as the primary proof, with textual indication (dalil al-nass) supporting.
5
Apply the rules to special cases
Consider the examples: silk requires weight specification; mixed fabrics (mulham, khazz) have specific rulings; hand-to-hand exchange of khazz cloth is only permissible by weight. Understand when weight is necessary.
These are mentioned in the later part of the passage from al-Bazzaziyya and al-Zahiriyya.

Source Text

واللبن والآجر إن سمي الخشبة
كتاب البيع باب السلم
ملبن معلوم والذرعي كالثوب إذا بين الذراع والصفة والصنعة لا في النيء وشرط في الخلاصة ذكر المكان الذي يعمل فيه اللبن، وفي الذخيرة: لو باع آجرة من ملبن لم تجز من غير إشارة لأن اللبن من المعاود المتقارب باعتبار قدره ومن المتفاوت باعتبار نضجه فاعتبر الأول في السلم للحاجة واعتبر الثاني في البيع قوله : (والآجر) بضم الجيم وتشديد الراء مع المد أشهر من التخفيف الواحدة آجرة وهو معرب وهو اللين إذا طبخ ؛ كذا في المصباح قوله : (إن) سمى ملبن معلوم) لأن آحادها لا تتفاوت إذا عينت الآلة وإذا لم تعين لا يجوز لإفضائه إلى المنازعة وفي المصباح : اللبن بكسر الباء ما يعلم من الطين يبنى به الواحدة لبنة ويجوز التخفيف فيصير مثل حمل ..اهـ. والملبن بكسر الباء قالب الطين والمحلب أيضاً ؛ كذا في الصحاح والمراد الأول قوله : ( والذرعي) أي ويصح السلم في المذروعات لأنه يمكن ضبطها بما ذكره، وجواز فيها بالإجماع كالثياب والبسط والحصر والبواري. وإنما جاز فيها مع أنها لم تذكر في النص وهو مشروع على خلاف القياس في المكيل والموزون فلا يقاس عليهما للإجماع ودلالة النص لأن سبب شرعيته الحاجة وهي لا تختلف قوله : (كالثوب إذا بين الذراع أي من أي جنس كذا ذكر العيني. وفي فتح القدير : أي قدره كذا كذا ذراعاً. وفي البزازية : إذا أطلق ذكر الذراع في الثوب فله ذراع وسط . وفي الذخيرة: واختلف المشايخ في تفسير قول محمد ذراع وسط ؛ منهم من And bricks and baked bricks if the mold is specified. The Book of Sales, Chapter of Salam. A known mold, and the cubit [measure] is like cloth when the cubit, description, and workmanship are specified, not in raw [state]. And in al-Khulasa, it is required to mention the place where the brick is made. And in al-Dhakhira: If someone sells a brick from a mold without indication, it is not permissible because bricks are close in size but vary in baking; so the former is considered in salam due to need, and the latter in sale. He said: (And al-ajar) with a dammah on the jim and tashdid on the ra with elongation, more famous than lightening; the singular is ajara; it is arabized and it is clay when baked. Thus in al-Misbah. He said: (If) he specifies a known mold, because its individuals do not differ when the tool is specified; if not specified, it is not permissible because it leads to dispute. And in al-Misbah: al-laban (with kasrah on the ba) is what is made from clay for building; the singular is labinah; lightening is permissible so it becomes like himl. The mold (malbin) with kasrah on the ba is the clay mold, and also the milking place; thus in al-Sihah; the first is meant. He said: (And the cubit measure) meaning salam is valid in items measured by cubit because they can be regulated by what was mentioned; its permissibility is by consensus, like clothes, rugs, mats, and reed mats. It is permitted even though it is not mentioned in the text, and it is legislated contrary to analogy in weighed and measured items, so it is not analogized to them due to consensus and textual evidence, because the reason for its legislation is need, which does not differ. He said: (Like cloth when the cubit is specified) meaning from any type, as mentioned by al-Ayni. And in Fath al-Qadir: meaning its length is such and such cubits. And in al-Bazzaziyya: If the mention of cubit is absolute for cloth, he has a middle cubit. And in al-Dhakhira: The scholars differed in interpreting Muhammad's statement 'middle cubit'; some said he meant the source, which is the act of cubit-measuring, not stretching fully nor letting go completely; some said he meant the stick; and the correct view is that it is applied to both if absolute, so he has the middle of both, considering both sides. He said: (And the description) meaning cotton or linen or a composite of both, which is mulham, or silk and the like. He said: (And the workmanship) meaning the work of Sham or Rum or Zayd, because it becomes known by mentioning these things, so it does not lead to dispute. And he did not mention weight because it is not a condition except for silk when sold by weight because it is only known by weight. And in al-Zahiriyya: Mentioning weight is not required for coarse cloth; they differed on silk, and the correct is that it is required. If one makes salam in a khazzan cloth specifying length, width, and pieces without mentioning weight, it is permissible; if he mentions only weight, it is not permissible. If one sells a khazz cloth for a khazz cloth hand to hand, it is not permissible except by weight because it is only sold by weight. And in al-Bazzaziyya: If one makes salam in Herati cotton for a Herati cloth, it is permissible; if one makes salam in hair cloth (mash) for hair cloth, if the mash is customary hair, it is not permissible; otherwise, it is permissible. Then he said regarding type: If one makes salam in a medium cloth and brings a good one and says 'take this and give me an extra dirham', its issues will come at his statement 'it is not permissible to dispose of the subject of salam before taking possession'.

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq (a commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq) explains the rulings of salam (advance payment sale) in items measured by cubit and bricks. The author begins with the condition for salam in bricks (laban and ajar): the mold (malbin) must be specified because bricks vary in size and baking. If unspecified, it leads to dispute. For items measured by cubit (madhru'at) like cloth, salam is valid by consensus despite being contrary to analogy (qiyas) because of public need. The text then details the required specifications: length (cubit), description (cotton, linen, etc.), and workmanship. The exact meaning of 'middle cubit' is discussed: some say it refers to moderate stretching, others to the measuring stick; the correct view is that both are considered. Weight is generally not required except for silk sold by weight. Special cases for mixed fabrics and currency exchanges are also mentioned.

Key Terms
ملبن (malbin): The mold used to form bricks; specifying it ensures uniformity.
ذراع (dhira'): Cubit, a unit of length; in salam it must be specified as 'middle cubit'.
صفة (sifah): Description of the material (e.g., cotton, linen).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Salam in bricks requires specifying the mold; in cubit-measured items, specifying cubit, description, and workmanship is necessary to prevent dispute and ensure validity.

The Prohibition of Salam in Animals and Their Limbs
Stating the prohibition of salam in animals and parts with proof and ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam in animals and their parts, identify the primary hadith evidence, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on limbs.

Core Idea
Salam in animals is prohibited by explicit hadith; limbs are also prohibited due to extreme disparity, though the two disciples permit.

Salam (advance payment sale) is a special contract where the price is paid upfront and the commodity is delivered later. However, not all commodities are suitable. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses salam in animals and their parts, establishing the general prohibition based on a prophetic hadith. It also reveals a subtle difference within the Hanafi school regarding animal limbs, which hinges on the degree of uncertainty (gharar).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and its legal status. The act is 'salam' (advance payment sale) in animals. The ruling is that it is invalid (batil) and haram.
The matn states clearly: 'Animals, and not its parts...' – meaning salam in animals is not valid.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the proof cited. The text quotes a hadith narrated by al-Hakim: the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited salam in animals.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain), so its thubut is zanni, but it is relied upon.
3
Understand the application to all animals
The text explicitly extends the prohibition even to sparrows, stating that the ruling is based on the text's wording, not on the presence of disparity.
This is a strict textualist approach: the 'illah (effective cause) is not considered; the text itself is the basis.
4
Note the exception of fresh fish
The passage mentions that fresh fish is an exception – salam in fish is permissible. This is a known ruling that will be discussed later.
The exception shows that not all animals are treated identically; fish have a different nature due to possibility of description.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on parts
The text states that animal parts (head, legs) are also prohibited due to 'gross disparity', but notes that according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad it is permissible. Understand the reasoning behind each view.
Abu Hanifa prohibits because parts cannot be precisely described; the two disciples permit if the parts are specified by number and type, reducing uncertainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحيوان ولا أطرافه كالرأس والأكارع والجلود عدداً والحطب خرماً والرطبة جرزاً والجوهر والخرز حتى لو كان عبداً فأعتقه يجوز لكونه مملوكاً له؛ ذكره الأسبيجابي، وقدمناه قبيل الربا. أطلقه فشمل الآدمي وغيره وقد صح أنه عليه السلام نهى عن السلف في الحيوان. رواه الحاكم وصححه. فشمل العصافير وإن لم يكن فيها تفاوت لأن الاعتبار في المنصوص عليه لعين النص لا للمعنى وهو لم يفصل ؛ كذا في الكافي. ولكنه يخرج عنه السمك الطري فإن السلم فيه جائز كما سيأتي ولكن في فتح القدير إن شرطت حياته فلنا إن نمنع صحته .
وهو
قوله : (ولا أطرافه كالرأس والأكارع لفحش التفاوت، وقيل عندهما يجوز. والأكارع جمع كراع للشاة والبقرة ويجمع على إكراع أيضاً
Animals, and not its parts like the head and legs, and hides by number, and firewood by bundles, and fodder by bundles, and gems and beads. Even if a slave and he emancipates him, it is permissible because he owns him; mentioned by al-Isbijabi, and we presented it before riba. It is absolute and includes humans and others. And it is authentically reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited salam (advance payment) in animals. Narrated by al-Hakim and authenticated. So it includes sparrows even if there is no disparity, because consideration in the text is for the text itself, not the meaning, and he did not differentiate. Thus in al-Kafi. But fresh fish is excluded, for salam in it is permissible as will come, but in Fath al-Qadir if its life is conditioned, we have [grounds] to deny its validity.
And his statement: (And not its parts like the head and legs) because of gross disparity, and it is said according to them (the two disciples) it is permissible. And al-akar' is plural of kur' for sheep and cow, and also plural is ikra'.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the prohibition of salam in animals and their parts. The matn states that salam is not valid for animals, their limbs (head, legs), hides, firewood, fodder, gems, and beads. The commentary explains that even if the commodity is a slave whom the buyer then frees, the contract is still valid because the slave was owned. The primary proof is a hadith narrated by al-Hakim: the Prophet (ﷺ) prohibited salam in animals. This is applied even to sparrows where there is no apparent disparity, because the ruling is based on the text's wording. Fresh fish is an exception, as salam in it is permissible. Regarding animal parts (limbs), there is disagreement: Abu Hanifa prohibits due to gross disparity, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two disciples) permit it under certain conditions. The text also defines 'akar' as legs of sheep and cows.

Key Terms
أكارع (akar'): Legs of sheep or cows; the text states they are prohibited due to gross disparity.
سلف (salaf): Synonym for salam (advance payment sale).
تفاوت (tafawut): Disparity or uncertainty in value; the reason for prohibition in animal parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qiyas on weighed items
B) A hadith in which the Prophet (ﷺ) prohibited it
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) The impossibility of describing animals

Key Takeaway
Salam in animals is prohibited by a clear prophetic hadith, and animal parts are also prohibited due to extreme disparity, though valid ikhtilaf exists within the Hanafi school.

Salam in Hides, Firewood, Fodder, Gems, and Intermittent Goods
Ruling on salam in various non-fungible commodities with expansion based on specification conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which salam is valid or invalid for hides, firewood, fodder, gems, and intermittent goods, and apply the rule of continuity of existence (munqati').

Core Idea
Salam in inherently variable goods requires precise specification; otherwise, it is invalid due to gharar.

This lesson continues the discussion of salam contracts, focusing on commodities that exhibit gross disparity (تفاوت فاحش) among their individuals. The author explains when such salam is invalid and when it becomes permissible through detailed specification of tanning, dimensions, weight, or other criteria. Understanding these conditions is crucial to avoid invalid contracts arising from uncertainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule for salam in non-fungible goods
Recognize that salam is intrinsically allowed only in fungible (mithli) goods; non-fungible goods like hides, firewood, and fresh fodder require exceptional conditions to be valid.
The default ruling for such goods is impermissibility due to gharar.
2
Categorize each commodity and its required specification
For each commodity (hides, firewood, ratbah, gems, intermittent goods), note the specific conditions listed in the text that make salam permissible (e.g., known tanning for hides, weight for firewood).
Conditions vary: some need dimensions, others need weight, some are never permissible (intermittent).
3
Understand the exception for hides and gems
Hides become permissible if tanning, dimensions, and quality are specified; gems are impermissible except for small pearls sold by weight.
The key is that specification reduces disparity to an acceptable level.
4
Apply the principle of continuity (munqati')
Salam in intermittent goods (منقطع) is invalid because the condition that the good exist from contract to delivery is missing.
This condition is separate from specification; it concerns the very existence of the good.
5
Recognize the role of custom in salam
The text notes that in certain lands, firewood is customarily sold by weight, making salam by weight valid and more precise.
Custom (urf) can determine permissible specifications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والجلود عدداً) أي لا يجوز السلم فيها للتفاوت الفاحش إلا أن يبين ضراباً معلوماً وطولاً وعرضاً وصفة معلومة من الجودة والرداءة فيجوز حينئذ عدداً ووزناً قوله : (والحطب حزماً والرطبة جرزاً) أي لا يجوز السلم فيها للتفاوت الفاحش لأنه مجهول لا يعرف طوله وغلظه حتى لو عرف ذلك بأن بين الحبل الذي يشد به الحطب والرطبة وبين طوله وضبط ذلك بحيث لا يؤدي إلى النزاع جاز، ولو قدر الوزن في الكل جاز، وفي ديارنا تعارفوا في نوع من الحطب الوزن فيجوز الإسلام فيه وزناً أضبط وأطيب ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الخلاصة ولا يجوز السلم في الحطب أوقاراً. والرطبة القضب خاصة ما دام رطباً والجمع رطاب؛ كذا في الصحاح. وفي المصباح: الجرزة القصبة القت ونحوه والحزمة والجمع جرز مثل غرفة وغرف، وأرض من جُرُز بضمتين قد انقطع الماء عنها فهي يابسة لإنبات فيها .اهـ. وفي الذخيرة: وأما الرياحين الرطبة والبقول والقصب والحشيش والخشب فهذه لم تكن مثلية فلا يجوز فيها، ولا بأس بالسلم في الجذوع إذا بين ضرباً معلوماً والطول والعرض والغلظ، وكذا الساج وصنوف العيدان. وفي البناية الرطبة الأسفست وهي التي تسميه أهل مصر برسيماً، وأهل البلاد القت لأنه الشمالية بنجا. وفي الشامل : لا خير في المسلم في الرطبة ويجوز في وزناً يباع قوله : (والجوهر والخرز) لتفاوت آحاده إلا صغار اللؤلؤ التي تباع وزناً يجوز السلم فيها وزناً لأنها تباع به فأمكن معرفة قدرها. والخَرَز بالتحريك الذي ينظم الواحدة خرزة وخرزات الملك جواهر تاجه ويقال كان الملك إذا ملك عاماً زيدت في تاجه خرزة ليعلم عدد سني ملكه ؛ كذا في الصحاح قوله : ( والمنقطع) أي لا يجوز السلم في الشيء المنقطع لفوت شرطه أن يكون موجوداً من حين العقد إلى حين المحل - بكسر الحاء - مصدر ميمي من الحلول وهو
وما بعده تعليل لدلالة النص. قوله: (ويجوز في القت) قال في الصحاح : القت الفصفصة والفصفصة بالكسر الرطبة : أبو السعود عن شيخه وفي القاموس ألقت تم الحديث كالتقتيت والقتيتي والإسفست ويابسه .
He said: (And hides by number) meaning salam in them is not permissible due to gross disparity unless one specifies a known tanning, length, width, and known description of quality and inferiority; then it is permissible by number and weight. He said: (And firewood by bundles and fodder by bundles) meaning salam in them is not permissible due to gross disparity because they are unknown in length and thickness; unless that is known by specifying the rope used to tie the firewood and the fodder, and specifying its length, and regulating it so that it does not lead to dispute, then it is permissible. And if weight is specified for all, it is permissible. And in our lands, they have customary weight for a type of firewood, so salam in it by weight is permissible, more precise and better. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Khulasa, salam in firewood by loads is not permissible. And al-ratbah is specifically the fodder (al-qadb) as long as it is moist; plural ratab. Thus in al-Sihah. And in al-Misbah: al-jurzah is the stalk of fodder (al-qat) and the like, and the bundle; plural jurz like ghurfah; and land with no water is juruz. And in al-Dhakhira: As for moist greens, vegetables, sugarcane, grass, and wood, these are not fungible (mithli) so salam in them is not permissible. There is no harm in salam in beams if one specifies a known type, length, width, and thickness; likewise for teak and types of wood. And in al-Binaya: al-ratbah is al-asfist, which the Egyptians call bersim, and the people of the country call it qat because it is the northern clover. And in al-Shamil: There is no good in salam in ratbah, and it is permissible by weight if sold. He said: (And gems and beads) due to the disparity of their individuals, except for small pearls that are sold by weight; salam in them is permissible by weight because they are sold by weight, so their quantity can be known. And al-kharaz (with fatha on the ra) is that which is strung; the singular is kharazah; the king's kharazat are the jewels of his crown; it is said that when the king ruled a year, a bead was added to his crown to know the number of years of his reign. Thus in al-Sihah. He said: (And what is intermittent) meaning salam is not permissible in an intermittent thing because its condition is lost, that it should exist from the time of the contract until the time of delivery (al-mahall with kasr on the ha, a verbal noun from hulul). And what follows is an explanation of the textual evidence. He said: (And it is permissible in al-qat). In al-Sihah: al-qat is alfalfa; and alfalfa with kasr is ratbah. Abu al-Su'ud from his teacher, and in al-Qamus: al-qat, the hadith is completed like al-taqtit and al-qittiti and al-isfast and its dry.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage continues the exposition of salam rulings in various commodities. For hides (جلود), salam is invalid due to gross disparity unless the specific tanning, dimensions, and quality are stated. For firewood (حطب) and fodder (رطبة), salam is invalid unless the rope length and bundle size are specified, or weight is used. Customary weight is acceptable. The text then clarifies that moist greens, vegetables, sugarcane, grass, and wood are not fungible, so salam in them is invalid; but beams and specific types of wood (like teak) are permissible if dimensions are given. For gems (جوهر) and beads (خرز), salam is invalid due to inherent variability, except for small pearls sold by weight. Finally, salam is invalid for intermittent goods (منقطع) that may not exist from contract to delivery. The term 'منقطع' refers to goods that may become unavailable. The passage ends with a note that salam is permissible in 'قت' (alfalfa), citing lexical sources.

Key Terms
منقطع (munqati'): A good that may become unavailable or intermittent; salam in it is invalid because it must exist from contract to delivery.
رطبة (ratbah): Fresh fodder (usually alfalfa or clover); salam invalid unless specified by weight or dimensions.
ضراب (dirab): The specific tanning or processing method used on hides; must be specified in salam to avoid gharar.
خرز (kharaz): Beads; salam in them is invalid due to disparity unless they are small pearls sold by weight.
تفاوت فاحش (tafawut fahish): Gross disparity or extreme variation among individuals of a commodity, rendering salam invalid unless specification eliminates it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) If the weight is specified

Key Takeaway
Salam in non-fungible goods is invalid due to gharar unless specific conditions (like tanning, dimensions, weight, or continuous availability) are met to remove uncertainty.

The Prohibition of Salam in Animals and the Exception for Fresh Fish
Ruling statement with textual proof and exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam in animals, cite the hadith evidence, and identify the exception for fresh fish along with its condition.

Core Idea
Salam in animals is haram by text; fresh fish is excepted due to custom but subject to life stipulation.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary clarifies a key ruling in salam (advance payment sale). While salam is generally valid, it is prohibited for animals due to a specific hadith. The commentator explains that the prohibition includes humans and even small animals like sparrows. However, an important exception is made for fresh fish, which is permissible, but with the note that if the fish's life is stipulated, the validity may be challenged.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is salam (salaf) in animals. The ruling is that it is prohibited and the contract is invalid (fasid).
This is the general rule; the exception is fresh fish.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the hadith: 'He (peace be upon him) prohibited salaf in animals' (نهى عن السلف في الحيوان). This hadith is narrated by al-Hakim and authenticated.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, a prohibition (nahy) indicates the invalidity (fasad) of the contract. The hadith's explicit prohibition makes salam in animals fasid.
The reasoning is that the text itself ('ayn al-nass) is considered, not the underlying rationale of disparity.
4
Note the scope
The ruling includes all animals, even humans and sparrows. The author's unrestricted wording covers all.
The commentator notes that the text does not differentiate, so even small animals are included.
5
Identify the exception and its condition
Fresh fish is exempted from the prohibition; salam in fresh fish is permissible. However, from Fath al-Qadir, if the fish's life is stipulated, there is a basis to prevent its validity.
This exception is based on custom and will be discussed later in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب السلم الحيوان ولا أطرافه كالرأس والأكارع والجلود عدداً والحطب خرماً والرطبة جرزاً والجوهر والخرز حتى لو كان عبداً فأعتقه يجوز لكونه مملوكاً له؛ ذكره الأسبيجابي، وقدمناه قبيل الربا. أطلقه فشمل الآدمي وغيره وقد صح أنه عليه السلام نهى عن السلف في الحيوان. رواه الحاكم وصححه. فشمل العصافير وإن لم يكن فيها تفاوت لأن الاعتبار في المنصوص عليه لعين النص لا للمعنى وهو لم يفصل ؛ كذا في الكافي. ولكنه يخرج عنه السمك الطري فإن السلم فيه جائز كما سيأتي ولكن في فتح القدير إن شرطت حياته فلنا إن نمنع صحته .
Book of Sales, Chapter of Salam. Animals and not its limbs like the head and shanks, and skins by count, and firewood by bundles, and fodder by bundles, and jewels and beads, even if it was a slave and he freed him, it is permissible because he is his property; al-Asbijabi mentioned it, and we presented it before riba. He (the author) made it unrestricted so it includes humans and others. And it is established that he (peace be upon him) prohibited salaf in animals. Narrated by al-Hakim and authenticated. So it includes sparrows even if there is no disparity because the consideration in the text is for the text itself, not for the meaning, and he did not differentiate; as in al-Kafi. But fresh fish is excluded from it, because salam in it is permissible as will come, but in Fath al-Qadir, if its life is stipulated, then we have [a basis] to prevent its validity.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It opens with the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq stating the prohibition of salam in animals and their parts, then focuses on animals. The commentator notes that the author's unrestricted wording includes humans, and cites the hadith of the Prophet prohibiting salaf in animals, reported by al-Hakim and authenticated. The reasoning is that the textual prohibition considers the text itself, not the underlying meaning of disparity. Thus, even sparrows, which may not have great disparity, are included. However, fresh fish is excluded from this prohibition, as salam in fish is permissible, to be discussed later. The commentator adds a note from Fath al-Qadir: if the life of the fish is stipulated, there is a basis to prevent its validity. This lesson establishes the general ruling on animals and notes a specific exception.

Key Terms
السلم (as-salam): A sale where the price (ra's al-mal) is paid in advance, and the commodity (muslam fihi) is delivered later. Also called salaf.
الحيوان (al-hayawan): Animals, including humans as per the commentator's note that the prohibition includes human beings.
السمك الطري (as-samak at-tari): Fresh fish, i.e., fish that is not dried or preserved; considered a commodity where salam is permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Because animals are always subject to price fluctuation.
D) Because animals are perishable goods.

Key Takeaway
Salam in animals is invalid based on prophetic prohibition; fresh fish is an exception, but stipulating life may challenge its validity.
