Salam in Animal Limbs and Skins: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
States prohibition of salam in limbs and skins with a minority view allowing it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of salam in animal limbs and skins according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the conditions that make salam in skins valid.

Core Idea
Salam in limbs is invalid per Abu Hanifa but permissible per Sahibayn; skins require detailed description.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a key detail in salam (forward sale) contracts: whether one can contract salam in animal parts like heads and shanks, and in skins by count. The default ruling is prohibition due to extreme disparity (fahsh al-tafawut), but an intra-Hanafi disagreement emerges: while Imam Abu Hanifa holds the prohibition, his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, consider it permissible. For skins, the prohibition can be overcome by specifying dimensions and quality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two subjects of the ruling
The matn mentions 'limbs' (al-atraf) like head and shanks, and 'skins by count'. Note that these are separate items with potentially different rulings.
Limbs are parts of animals; skins are primarily used for leather.
2
Parse the matn's default ruling for limbs
The phrase 'ولا أطرافه' indicates that salam in limbs is not permissible. The reason given is 'li-fahsh al-tafawut' (due to extreme disparity). Identify this as Abu Hanifa's position.
Extreme disparity means limbs vary greatly in size, weight, and quality, making specification uncertain.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement on limbs
The phrase 'وقيل عندهما يجوز' indicates that according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), salam in limbs is permissible. Distinguish that this is a legitimate difference within the Hanafi school.
'عندهما' is a standard reference to the two disciples.
4
Examine the ruling for skins
The matn says 'والجلود عدداً' meaning salam in skins by count is not permissible. However, the commentary clarifies that if the seller specifies the type (e.g., ram), length, width, and quality, then it becomes permissible by count and weight.
Thus, skins require a detailed description to remove the disparity.
5
Trace the practical consequence (thamarah)
Under Abu Hanifa, a salam contract for a sheep's head or shanks is invalid; under the Sahibayn, it is valid if adequately described. For skins, valid only if detailed conditions are met.
This difference affects the validity of many salam contracts in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو قوله : (ولا أطرافه كالرأس والأكارع والجلود عدداً والحطب حزماً والرطبة جرزاً والجوهر والخرز قوله : (ولا أطرافه كالرأس والأكارع لفحش التفاوت، وقيل عندهما يجوز. والأكارع جمع كراع للشاة والبقرة ويجمع على إكراع أيضاً قوله : ( والجلود عدداً) أي لا يجوز السلم فيها للتفاوت الفاحش إلا أن يبين ضراباً معلوماً وطولاً وعرضاً وصفة معلومة من الجودة والرداءة فيجوز حينئذ عدداً ووزناً
And it is His saying: 'And not its limbs like the head and shanks and skins by count, and firewood by bundles, and fodder by bundles, and jewels and beads.' [Then:] His saying: 'And not its limbs like the head and shanks due to extreme disparity, and it is said according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that it is permissible.' Al-akari' is plural of kurā' for sheep and cow, and also pluralized as ikrā'. His saying: 'And skins by count' means salam in them is not permissible due to extreme disparity unless he specifies a known ram, length, width, and known quality of good and bad, then it is permissible by count and weight.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. It explains the matn's ruling on salam in limbs and skins. For limbs (like head and shanks), the default ruling is prohibition due to extreme disparity (fahsh al-tafawut). However, it is reported that according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), salam in limbs is permissible. The commentator defines 'al-akari' as the plural of kurā' (shank) for sheep and cow. For skins, salam is invalid by default due to extreme disparity, but if the seller specifies the type (e.g., ram), length, width, and quality, then it is permissible by count and weight. Thus, the conditions for validity are more detailed for skins. This shows an intra-Hanafi disagreement on limbs.

Key Terms
الأكارع (al-akaari'): Plural of kurā' (كراع), meaning the shanks of sheep or cows, from the elbow to the hoof.
الجلود (al-julud): Skins, plural of jild. Here, salam in skins by count is invalid unless detailed description is given.
عندهما (indahumā): According to the two (i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Salam in animal limbs is invalid per Abu Hanifa but permissible per Sahibayn; salam in skins requires detailed specification of type, dimensions, and quality to be valid.

Salam in Firewood and Fodder: Conditions for Validity
Ruling statement with conditions for validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that make salam in firewood and fodder valid and distinguish between valid and invalid salam based on specification.

Core Idea
Salam in firewood and fodder is invalid by default but valid when specified by dimensions or weight.

Salam (forward sale) requires that the subject matter be precisely known to avoid uncertainty. Firewood and fresh fodder are typically non-fungible and vary greatly, so the Hanafi school deems salam in them invalid unless the parties eliminate disparity through detailed specification or by using weight. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the default prohibition and the conditions that make it permissible, including the role of custom (urf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The passage begins by stating that salam in firewood by bundles and fodder by bundles is not permissible due to extreme disparity (al-tafāwut al-fāḥish) because their length and thickness are unknown.
The key term 'tafāwut fāḥish' refers to excessive uncertainty that invalidates the contract.
2
Find the condition that makes it valid
The ruling changes if the rope used to tie the bundle and the dimensions (length, thickness) are specified so precisely that no dispute arises. Then salam becomes permissible.
Specification removes the uncertainty, making the quantity known.
3
Note the alternative method: weight
If the firewood or fodder is weighed, salam becomes permissible because weight standardizes the quantity. The commentator notes that in his region (Egypt), custom (urf) has established weighing for a type of firewood, making salam by weight even better (aḍbaṭ wa aṭyab).
Custom can define the standard for validity.
4
Recognize the concept of mithli (fungibility)
The passage cites al-Dhakhira: fresh herbs, vegetables, hay, and wood are not mithli (fungible), so salam is generally invalid in them. This explains why specification is necessary—they cannot be replaced by identical units.
Fungibility (mithli) is a key concept in salam; only fungibles are eligible by default.
5
Apply to logs and other wood
For logs (judhūʿ), salam is valid if the type, length, width, and thickness are clearly stated. This shows the general principle: specification of measurable attributes permits salam even in non-fungibles.
Logs are like firewood but can be specified more easily.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والحطب حزماً والرطبة جرزاً) أي لا يجوز السلم فيها للتفاوت الفاحش لأنه مجهول لا يعرف طوله وغلظه حتى لو عرف ذلك بأن بين الحبل الذي يشد به الحطب والرطبة وبين طوله وضبط ذلك بحيث لا يؤدي إلى النزاع جاز، ولو قدر الوزن في الكل جاز، وفي ديارنا تعارفوا في نوع من الحطب الوزن فيجوز الإسلام فيه وزناً أضبط وأطيب ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الخلاصة ولا يجوز السلم في الحطب أوقاراً. والرطبة القضب خاصة ما دام رطباً والجمع رطاب؛ كذا في الصحاح. وفي المصباح: الجرزة القصبة القت ونحوه والحزمة والجمع جرز مثل غرفة وغرف، وأرض من جُرُز بضمتين قد انقطع الماء عنها فهي يابسة لإنبات فيها .اهـ. وفي الذخيرة: وأما الرياحين الرطبة والبقول والقصب والحشيش والخشب فهذه لم تكن مثلية فلا يجوز فيها، ولا بأس بالسلم في الجذوع إذا بين ضرباً معلوماً والطول والعرض والغلظ، وكذا الساج وصنوف العيدان. وفي البناية الرطبة الأسفست وهي التي تسميه أهل مصر برسيماً، وأهل البلاد القت لأنه الشمالية بنجا. وفي الشامل : لا خير في المسلم في الرطبة ويجوز في وزناً يباع
His saying: 'And firewood by bundles and fodder by bundles' means salam in them is not permissible due to extreme disparity because it is unknown, not known in length and thickness. If that is known by specifying the rope with which the firewood and fodder are tied and specifying its length and controlling it so that it does not lead to dispute, then it is permissible. And if weight is determined in all, it is permissible. And in our lands, they have become accustomed to a type of firewood by weight, so salam in it is permissible by weight, which is more precise and better; as in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Khulasa: salam in firewood by loads (awqār) is not permissible. Al-ratbah specifically refers to fresh fodder (al-qadab) as long as it is fresh, plural ratāb; as in al-Sihah. In al-Misbah: al-jurza is a bundle of hay and the like, and the bundle, plural jurz like ghurfa and ghuraf, and land of jurz (two dammas) meaning water ceased from it so it is dry and does not allow vegetation. In al-Dhakhira: as for fresh herbs, vegetables, sugarcane, hay, and wood, these are not fungible (mithli), so salam in them is not permissible. There is no problem in salam in logs if he specifies a known type, length, width, and thickness, and likewise teak and types of wood. In al-Binaya: al-ratbah is al-asfust, which the people of Egypt call barsīm, and the people of the lands call al-qatt because it is the northern al-banja. In al-Shamil: there is no good in salam in al-ratbah, and it is permissible by weight as it is sold.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with conditions. It explains that salam in firewood (hatab) and fodder (ratbah) is generally invalid because their size and weight are unknown, leading to extreme disparity. However, if the seller specifies the rope size and the dimensions precisely to avoid dispute, then salam becomes valid. Additionally, if the items are weighed, they become determined and salam is valid. The commentator notes that in his region (Egypt), custom (urf) has established weight for a type of firewood, so salam by weight is permissible and even preferred. He then provides lexical definitions: 'ratbah' is specifically fresh fodder (qadab), and its plural is ratāb. The word 'jurza' means a bundle of hay or similar. He also cites al-Dhakhira that fresh herbs, vegetables, hay, and wood are not fungible (mithli), so salam is invalid in them generally, but logs can be subject to salam if type and dimensions are specified. He also mentions that al-ratbah is called 'asfust' or 'barsim' (alfalfa) in Egypt, and in other regions it is called 'al-qatt' (clover). The overall ruling is that salam in these items is invalid by default but becomes valid with precise description, particularly by weight.

Key Terms
الرطبة (ar-ratbah): Fresh fodder or clover, called barsim in Egypt and al-qatt in other regions.
الجرزة (al-jurza): A bundle of hay or similar, plural jurz.
مثلي (mithli): Fungible goods that can be replaced by similar items. The passage states that fresh herbs etc. are not mithli, so salam is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which condition makes salam in firewood and fodder valid?
A) Paying a higher price.
B) Specifying the rope size, length, and controlling to avoid dispute.
C) Being fresh at the time of contract.
D) Using a standard bundle size.

Key Takeaway
Salam in non-fungible items like firewood is invalid unless the quantity is precisely determined by specification of dimensions or weight.

Salam in Jewels and Beads: Exception for Small Pearls
States prohibition of salam in jewelry and beads due to disparity, but allows for small pearls sold by weight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for salam in jewelry and beads, identify the exception for small pearls, and explain why weight-based sale resolves the disparity.

Core Idea
Salam requires knowable quantity; jewels and beads are too disparate, but small pearls sold by weight become knowable.

Salam is an advance payment sale where the subject matter must be precisely known in kind, quantity, and quality. Jewels and beads are each unique, making them unsuitable. However, small pearls sold by weight are fungible enough to allow salam. Let's parse the ruling from the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling
Read the initial part: 'والجوهر والخرز لتفاوت آحاده'. The ruling is that salam in jewels and beads is invalid due to the disparity of individual items.
Disparity means each piece differs in value, so quantity cannot be precisely defined.
2
Spot the Exception
Look for 'إلا صغار اللؤلؤ التي تباع وزناً'. The exception is for small pearls that are sold by weight.
The word 'إلا' signals a clear exception.
3
Understand the Rationale
The text says: 'يجوز السلم فيها وزناً لأنها تباع به فأمكن معرفة قدرها'. The reason for permissibility is that being sold by weight makes the quantity knowable.
Knowability (ma'rifat al-qadr) is essential for salam.
4
Lexical Note on Kharaz
The commentator explains that 'al-kharaz' (beads) are strung items, singular kharaza, and gives a historical anecdote about kings adding beads to crowns.
This lexical clarification helps define the term accurately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والجوهر والخرز) لتفاوت آحاده إلا صغار اللؤلؤ التي تباع وزناً يجوز السلم فيها وزناً لأنها تباع به فأمكن معرفة قدرها. والخَرَز بالتحريك الذي ينظم الواحدة خرزة وخرزات الملك جواهر تاجه ويقال كان الملك إذا ملك عاماً زيدت في تاجه خرزة ليعلم عدد سني ملكه ؛ كذا في الصحاح
His saying: 'And jewels and beads' due to the disparity of their individuals, except for small pearls that are sold by weight; salam in them is permissible by weight because they are sold by it, so knowing their measure is possible. And al-kharaz (with vowelization) is what is strung, the singular is kharaza, and the king's kharazat are the jewels of his crown. It is said that when a king ruled for a year, a kharaza was added to his crown to indicate the number of years of his reign; as in al-Sihah.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with an exception. It states that salam in jewels (jawhar) and beads (kharaz) is invalid because each piece is unique, leading to disparity in value. However, small pearls that are sold by weight are an exception: salam in them is permissible by weight because they are sold by weight, making it possible to know their quantity. The commentator then provides a lexical definition of 'kharaz', explaining that it refers to strung beads, and gives a historical anecdote about kings adding a bead to their crown for each year of reign. This ruling emphasizes that the default prohibition can be overcome when the items are measurable by weight.

Key Terms
الجوهر (al-jawhar): Jewels, precious stones, each piece unique.
الخرز (al-kharaz): Beads used for stringing; singular kharaza.
صغار اللؤلؤ (sighar al-lu'lu'): Small pearls sold by weight, which are fungible enough for salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is salam in small pearls by weight permissible according to this passage?
A) Because they are expensive.
B) Because they are sold by weight, allowing knowledge of quantity.
C) Because they are naturally uniform.
D) Because they are not considered jewelry.

Key Takeaway
Salam in items with individual disparity is invalid, but if the items are sold by weight, the quantity becomes knowable and salam is valid.

Salam in Intermittent Items, Fish, and Meat: Conditions and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salam in meat with ancillary rulings on intermittent items and fish.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid salam in fish and meat, and explain why the Hanafi school has an internal dispute on meat.

Core Idea
Salam requires the item to exist and be measurable; meat's variability creates an intra-Hanafi split on its permissibility.

This passage from Bahru al-Ra'iq presents the Hanafi rulings on salam in items that are seasonal or variable. The main focus is the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding salam in meat. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how conditions of existence and measurement operate in salam contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for salam
Recognize that salam requires the item to exist from the time of contract to the time of delivery (mahall). If the item disappears during this period, the contract is invalid due to uncertainty and potential loss.
This is a fundamental condition for all salam contracts.
2
Apply to intermittent items (al-munqati')
Analyze why intermittent items are invalid: they are not available at delivery, so the condition fails. The text gives this as a clear example.
3
Distinguish fresh vs salted fish
Fresh fish is seasonal; invalid during winter when it disappears. Salted fish (malih) is preserved and measurable by weight, so valid. Note the role of season and measurability.
Even fresh fish can be valid if contract and delivery are within its season.
4
Examine the meat dispute
Identify the core issue: meat varies by bone size, fatness, and season. Abu Hanifa says this leads to excessive uncertainty (gharar fahish), invalidating the contract. Sahibayn argue that precise description (weight, type, age, cut) removes the uncertainty, making it permissible by analogy to fat (alya).
This is the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Determine the fatwa position
The text cites al-Haqa'iq and al-Uyun: the fatwa is on the view of the two (Sahibayn). So the operative ruling permits salam in meat if all attributes are specified.
De-boned meat (makhlu' al-azm) has a separate narration; the more correct view is invalidity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والمنقطع) أي لا يجوز السلم في الشيء المنقطع لفوت شرطه أن يكون موجوداً من حين العقد إلى حين المحل - بكسر الحاء - مصدر ميمي من الحلول وهو والمنقطع ولا في السمك الطري وصح وزناً لو مالحاً ولا يصح السلم في اللحم وبمكيال أو كان قوله : (ولا في السمك الطري) أي لا يجوز فيه لأنه ينقطع عن أيدي الناس في الشتاء لانجماد المياه حتى لو كان في وقت لا ينقطع فيه جاز وزناً لا عدداً. والحاصل كما في شرح الطحاوي أنه إما أن يكون طرياً أو مالحاً، ولا يخلو إما أن يسلم عدداً أو وزناً، فإن أسلم فيه مطلقاً للتفاوت، وإن أسلم فيه وزناً ؛ فإن كان مملوحاً يجوز، وإن كان طرياً فإن كان العقد في حينه والحلول في حينه ولا ينقطع فيما بينهما جاز وإلا فلا قوله : (وصح وزناً لو مالحاً) أي صح السلم في السمك بالوزن لو كان ملحاً لا عدداً لأن الملح منه وهو القديد لا ينقطع وهو معلوم يمكن ضبطه ببيان قدره بالوزن وبیان نوعه بأن يقول بوري أوراي وفي أسماك الاسكندرية الشفس والدونيس وغيرها. وفي الإيضاح : الصحيح أن في الصغار منه يجوز وزناً وكيلاً وفي الكبار روايتان. وفي المغرب : سمك مليح ومملوح وهو القديد الذي فيه الملح ولا يقال مالح إلا في لغة رديئة والمالح هو الذي شق بطنه وجعل فيه الملح قوله: (ولا يصح السلم في اللحم أي عند أبي حنيفة وقالا يجوز إذا بين جنسه ونوعه وسنة وموضعه وصفته وقدره كشاة خصي ثني سمين من الجنب أو الفخذ مائة رطل لأنه موزون مضبوط الوصف فصار كالألية والشحم بخلاف لحم الطيور فإنه لا يقدر على وصف موضع منه وله أن يختلف باختلاف كبر العظم وصغره فيؤدي إلى المنازعة. وفي منزوع العظم روايتان والأصح عدمه ولذا أطلقه في الكتاب. وفي الحقائق والعيون: الفتوى على قولهما عدداً لم يحز قوله : (وله أنه يختلف باختلاف كبر العظم وصغره قال في الفتح: وعلى هذا الوجه يجوز السلم في مخلوع العظم وهو رواية الحسن عنه ، ثم ذكر للإمام وجهاً آخر وهو أنه يختلف بحسب الفصول سمناً وهزالاً قال : وحاصل هذا الوجه أنه سلم في المنقطع وعلى هذا لا يجوز في مخلوع
His saying: 'And the intermittent' means salam is not permissible in the intermittent item because its condition is lost that it should exist from the time of contract to the time of delivery (mahall, with kasr of ha, a verbal noun from halūl), and it is: 'And the intermittent, and not in fresh fish, and it is correct by weight if it is salted, and salam in meat is not valid by measure or weight.' His saying: 'And not in fresh fish' means it is not permissible because it disappears from people's hands in winter due to freezing of waters, so if it is in a season when it does not disappear, it is permissible by weight, not by count. The summary in Sharh al-Tahawi: either it is fresh or salted, and it is either by count or weight. If he made salam absolutely (without specifying), [it is invalid] due to disparity; if by weight, then if it is salted, it is permissible, if fresh, then if the contract is in its season and delivery is in its season and it does not disappear in between, it is permissible, otherwise not. His saying: 'And it is correct by weight if it is salted' means salam in fish by weight is correct if it is salted, not by count, because the salted one is the salted fish (al-qadid) which does not disappear and is known, can be controlled by stating its weight and type, saying 'mullet' or 'rai' and among the fish of Alexandria: 'shafs' and 'dunis' etc. In al-Idah: the correct view is that in the small ones it is permissible by weight and volume, in the large ones two narrations. In al-Mughrib: samak malīh and mumallāh is the qadid that has salt, and it is not called mālih except in a poor language. Al-mālih is the one whose belly is cut and salt is placed. His saying: 'And salam in meat is not valid' according to Abu Hanifa, and the two said: it is permissible if he specifies its genus, type, age, place, description, and quantity, like a castrated two-year-old fat sheep from the side or thigh, one hundred ratls, because it is a weighed item with precise description, so it becomes like the fat tail and fat, contrary to bird meat because one cannot describe a part of it, and it can differ by size of bone, leading to dispute. Regarding de-boned meat, there are two narrations, the most correct is its invalidity, therefore the author (of Kanz) left it general. In al-Haqa'iq and al-Uyun: the fatwa is on the view of the two (Sahibayn). [The author's] saying: 'because it differs by size of bone' – he said in al-Fath: on this basis, salam in meat with bone removed is permissible, and it is a narration from al-Hasan from him. Then he mentioned for the Imam another aspect: that it differs by seasons, fatness and leanness. He said: the summary of this aspect is that it is salam in an intermittent item, and on this basis it is not permissible in de-boned meat.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. It covers three distinct rulings from the matn: (1) salam in intermittent items (al-munqati'), (2) salam in fresh and salted fish, and (3) salam in meat. For intermittent items, salam is invalid because the item must exist from the time of contract to delivery; if it disappears, it leads to uncertainty and potential loss. For fish: fresh fish is invalid because it disappears in winter; however, in seasons of availability, it is permissible by weight, not by count. Salted fish is valid by weight because it is preserved and measurable. For meat: there is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Abu Hanifa holds that salam in meat is invalid because meat varies greatly (by bone size, fatness, etc.) making precise description impossible, leading to dispute. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold it is valid if all attributes are specified: genus, age, body part, weight, etc. They analogize it to other weighed commodities like fat (alya) and suet (shahm). The passage also discusses meat with bone removed (makhlu' al-azm): there is a narration from al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa allowing it, but the text notes that if the variation by season is considered, it becomes like an intermittent item and is invalid. The fatwa according to some sources is on the view of the Sahibayn, i.e., permissible with detailed description.

Key Terms
المنقطع (al-munqati'): An item that is seasonally unavailable, disappearing from the market between contract and delivery.
السمك الطري (as-samak at-tari): Fresh fish, not salted. Ruling: invalid except when in season and by weight.
الملح (al-malih): Salted fish (qadid). Valid for salam by weight.
اللحم (al-lahm): Meat. Disputed: Abu Hanifa invalid, Sahibayn valid with specification.
مخلوع العظم (makhlu' al-azm): De-boned meat. Two narrations, the most correct is invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the fatwa (operative ruling) regarding salam in meat?
A) It is invalid in all cases, following Abu Hanifa.
B) It is permissible if described in detail, following the Sahibayn.
C) It is valid only if de-boned.
D) It is invalid during winter.

Key Takeaway
Salam in meat is permissible in Hanafi fatwa if all attributes are precisely specified, despite Abu Hanifa's original objection due to variability.

Condition of Continuous Availability in Salam
Ruling on salam in discontinued commodities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of continuous availability (ittisal) in a salam contract, apply it to determine validity, and explain the buyer's option when the commodity becomes unavailable after the due date.

Core Idea
Salam is valid only if the commodity is continuously available from contract to delivery; post-due-date discontinuity gives the buyer an option, not automatic rescission.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on salam (advance purchase) in commodities that are not continuously available. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains that the commodity must be available in the market from the time of contract until delivery. Discontinuity at any point invalidates the contract. However, if it becomes unavailable after the due date, the buyer may choose to rescind or wait. We will also explore an intra-Hanafi difference on whether the contract is automatically rescinded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a salam contract (advance purchase of a described commodity). The ruling depends on the condition of continuous availability. If the commodity is discontinued at any time before delivery, the contract is invalid (batil).
The condition applies from contract formation until the delivery date.
2
Define discontinuity (inqita')
Discontinuity means the commodity is not found in the markets where it is usually sold, even if available in private homes. This definition prevents uncertainty (gharar) in delivery.
The standard is market availability, not absolute existence.
3
Apply the rule to different scenarios
The text states that salam is invalid if the commodity is discontinued at contract but available at delivery, or vice versa, or discontinued in between. Also, if discontinued in one region but available in another, salam is invalid in the region where absent due to hardship.
Regional unavailability is treated as discontinuity.
4
Note the exception after the due date
If the commodity becomes unavailable after the delivery date (but before actual delivery), the contract is not automatically void. The buyer (rabb al-salam) has the option (khiyar) to either rescind the contract and take back the capital, or wait for availability.
This differs from pre-delivery discontinuity which renders the contract invalid.
5
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
A narration from Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the contract is automatically rescinded (yantafikh) upon post-due-date discontinuity, but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the buyer has an option, as recorded in al-Bazzaziyya.
The mufta bihi aligns with the majority of the sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب السلم والمنقطع ولا في السمك الطري وصح وزناً لو مالحاً ولا يصح السلم في اللحم وبمكيال أو ذراع لم يدر قدره وبر قربة أو تمر نخلة معينة وشرطه بيان الجنس والنوع والصفة والقدر. قوله: (والمنقطع) حتى لو كان منقطعاً عند العقد موجوداً عند المحل أو بالعكس أو منقطعاً فيما بين ذلك لم يجز لأنه غير مقدور التسليم لتوهم موت المسلم إليه فيحل الأجل وهو منقطع فيتضرر رب السلم. وحد الانقطاع أن لا يوجد في الأسواق التي تباع فيها وإن كان في البيوت، ولو انقطع عن أيدي الناس بعد المحل قبل أن يوفي المسلم فيه فرب السلم بالخيار إن شاء فسخ العقد وأخذ رأس ماله، وإن شاء انتظر وجوده. وفي البناية معزياً إلى مبسوط أبي اليسر : ولو انقطع في إقليم دون إقليم لا يصح السلم في الإقليم الذي لا يوجد فيه لأنه لا يمكن إحضاره إلا بمشقة عظيمة فيعجز عن التسليم حتى لو أسلم في الرطب ببخارى لا يجوز وإن يوجد بسجستان اهـ. وفي البزازية : انقطع المسلم فيه في أوانه يتخير رب السلم. وعن الإمام أنه ينفسخ .اهـ. وفيها : استقرض فاكهة كيلاً أو وزناً ثم انقطع يصير إلى أن تدخل الجديدة إلا أن يتراضيا على قيمته كمن استقرض طعاماً في بلد فيه الطعام رخيص ثم التقيا في بلد فيه الطعام غال ليس له الطلب بل يوثق المطلوب ليعطيه في تلك البلد اهـ.
Chapter of Salam and the Discontinued. And not in fresh fish, and it is valid by weight if salted, and salam in meat is not valid, and with a measure or cubit whose capacity is not known, and with a water skin of a specific village or dates of a specific palm tree, and its condition is the clarification of type, kind, description, and quantity. He said: (and the discontinued): even if it is discontinued at the time of contract but available at the time of delivery, or vice versa, or discontinued in between, it is not permissible because it is not possible to deliver due to the possibility of the death of the one to whom salam was given, so the term becomes due and it is discontinued, thus the owner of the salam suffers loss. The definition of discontinuation is that it is not found in the markets where it is sold, even if it is in houses. If it disappears from people's hands after the time of delivery before the delivery of the salam commodity, then the owner of the salam has the option: if he wishes, he may rescind the contract and take back his capital; if he wishes, he may wait for its availability. In al-Binaya, attributed to Mabsoot of Abi al-Yusr: If it is discontinued in one region but not another, salam is not valid in the region where it is not available because it cannot be brought except with great hardship, so he is unable to deliver. Even if one makes salam in fresh dates in Bukhara, it is not permissible even though it is found in Sijistan. In al-Bazzaziyya: If the salam commodity is discontinued in its season, the owner of the salam has the choice. It is narrated from the Imam (Abu Hanifa) that it is rescinded. In it: He borrowed fruit by measure or weight, then it was discontinued; it becomes (like) until the new fruit enters unless they mutually agree on its value, like the one who borrows food in a town where food is cheap, then they meet in a town where food is expensive; the borrower does not have the right to demand, rather the lender is bound to give it in that town.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage discusses the condition of continuity (ittisal) in salam contracts. The commentator explains that salam is only valid if the commodity is normally available in the market from the time of contract until the due date. If it is unavailable at any point (whether at contract, at delivery, or in between), the contract is invalid because the seller cannot guarantee delivery. The definition of 'discontinued' is that it is not found in the markets where it is sold, even if available in private homes. If the commodity becomes unavailable after the due date but before delivery, the buyer has an option to either rescind the contract and get his money back, or wait for it to become available. A quote from al-Binaya adds that if the commodity is unavailable in one region but available in another, salam is invalid in the region where it is absent due to hardship in procurement. Another quote from al-Bazzaziyya notes that if the commodity is discontinued in its season, the buyer has a choice; a narration from Abu Hanifa says the contract is automatically rescinded. An example is given of borrowing fruit: if the fruit becomes scarce, the borrower must return the like when available unless they agree on value.

Key Terms
المنقطع (al-munqati'): A commodity that is not continuously available in the market from contract to delivery.
رب السلم (rabb al-salam): The buyer who pays the price in advance (the capital owner).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a salam commodity is available at the time of contract and at the time of delivery but not in between, what is the ruling according to the text?
A) The contract is valid because it is available at both ends.
B) The contract is not valid because it was discontinued in between.
C) The contract is valid but the buyer has an option.
D) The contract is automatically rescinded.

Key Takeaway
Salam requires continuous market availability from contract to delivery; post-due-date discontinuity gives the buyer a choice, not automatic rescission.

Salam in Fresh vs Salted Fish: Conditions of Validity
Ruling on salam in fresh and salted fish with conditions of validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam in fresh and salted fish and apply the condition of continuous availability to determine validity.

Core Idea
Fresh fish salam invalid unless both contract and due dates are in season; salted fish salam valid by weight.

The salam contract requires that the subject matter be known, specifiable, and continuously available until delivery. Fish presents a special case: fresh fish disappears in winter, while salted fish remains available. This lesson examines how these differences shape the Hanafi ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Recognize that the act is a salam contract (forward sale) for fish, which can be either fresh (tariyy) or salted (malih).
Salam is a sale with deferred delivery and immediate payment.
2
Distinguish fresh vs salted fish
Fresh fish is perishable and seasonally unavailable; salted fish (qadid) is preserved and continuously available.
This distinction is the key to the ruling.
3
Apply the condition of continuity (dawam)
For salam to be valid, the item must exist and be deliverable from contract to due date. Fresh fish fails this unless both dates fall within its season.
If the fish disappears in between, the contract involves risk (gharar) and is invalid.
4
Determine the mode of specification
Salam can be by count or by weight. For fresh fish, weight is the only valid mode; count is invalid due to size variation. For salted fish, weight is required.
Specification by weight ensures knowledge and eliminates uncertainty.
5
State the ruling and note the ikhtilaf
Fresh fish: invalid unless in season and continuous; valid only by weight. Salted fish: valid by weight, not by count. For large salted fish, there are two narrations (permissibility vs. prohibition).
The relied-upon view permits small salted fish by weight and measure, while caution is advised for large.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا في السمك الطري) أي لا يجوز فيه لأنه ينقطع عن أيدي الناس في الشتاء لانجماد المياه حتى لو كان في وقت لا ينقطع فيه جاز وزناً لا عدداً. والحاصل كما في شرح الطحاوي أنه إما أن يكون طرياً أو مالحاً، ولا يخلو إما أن يسلم عدداً أو وزناً، فإن أسلم فيه مطلقاً للتفاوت، وإن أسلم فيه وزناً ; فإن كان مملوحاً يجوز، وإن كان طرياً فإن كان العقد في حينه والحلول في حينه ولا ينقطع فيما بينهما جاز وإلا فلا قوله : (وصح وزناً لو مالحاً) أي صح السلم في السمك بالوزن لو كان ملحاً لا عدداً لأن الملح منه وهو القديد لا ينقطع وهو معلوم يمكن ضبطه ببيان قدره بالوزن وبیان نوعه بأن يقول بوري أوراي وفي أسماك الاسكندرية الشفس والدونيس وغيرها. وفي الإيضاح : الصحيح أن في الصغار منه يجوز وزناً وكيلاً وفي الكبار روايتان. وفي المغرب : سمك مليح ومملوح وهو القديد الذي فيه الملح ولا يقال مالح إلا في لغة رديئة والمالح هو الذي شق بطنه وجعل فيه الملح.
He said: ('and not in fresh fish') meaning it is not permissible because it disappears from people's hands in winter due to freezing of waters, to the extent that if it is a time when it does not disappear, then it is permissible by weight, not by count. The conclusion is as in Sharh al-Tahawi: it is either fresh or salted, and inevitably either the salam is by count or by weight. If he makes salam in it absolutely (without specification), it is invalid due to disparity. If he makes salam in it by weight, then if it is salted, it is permissible; if it is fresh, then if the contract is in its season and the due date is in its season and it does not disappear in between, it is permissible, otherwise not. He said: ('and it is valid by weight if salted') meaning salam in fish is valid by weight if it is salted, not by count, because the salted fish, which is qadid (dried salted fish), does not disappear and it is known and can be specified by stating its weight and type, such as 'buri' or 'rai', and in Alexandria fish there is shalfis and dunis and others. In al-Idah: the correct view is that in small fish it is permissible by weight and by measure, and in large fish there are two narrations. In al-Mughrib: samak malih and mumallah is the qadid that has salt, and it is not called malih except in a bad language; al-malih is that which has its belly slit and salt placed in it.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on salam in fish. The commentator begins by quoting the matn clause 'ولا في السمك الطري' (and not in fresh fish). The reason given is that fresh fish is not continuously available; it disappears in winter when waters freeze. However, if it is a time when it does not disappear (such as certain seasons or places), then salam in fresh fish is permissible by weight but not by count. The explanation from Sharh al-Tahawi breaks it down: fish is either fresh or salted; salam can be by count or by weight. If the salam is absolute (without specifying count or weight), it is invalid because of disparity. If it is by weight, then salted fish is always permissible because it does not disappear and is specifiable by weight and type. For fresh fish, it is permissible only if both the contract and due date fall within the season of availability and the fish does not disappear in between. The matn also states 'وصح وزناً لو مالحاً' (and it is valid by weight if salted). The commentator elaborates that salted fish (qadid) is known and can be specified by weight and type, giving examples of fish names. He cites a difference in small vs. large fish: in small fish it is permissible by weight and by measure (kayl), while in large fish there are two narrations (presumably permissibility and impermissibility). Finally, a linguistic note from al-Mughrib distinguishes between 'malih' and 'mumallah'.

Key Terms
السمك الطري (al-samak al-tariyy): Fresh fish, which is not preserved and subject to seasonal unavailability.
السمك المالح (al-samak al-malih): Salted dried fish (qadid), which does not disappear and is specifiable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is salam in fresh fish permissible according to the text?
A) It is always permissible by weight.
B) It is never permissible.
C) It is permissible if both contract and due date are in season and it does not disappear in between.
D) It is permissible if specified by count and type.

Key Takeaway
Fresh fish salam is invalid unless seasonally continuous; salted fish salam is always valid by weight, with caution for large varieties.

Salam in Meat: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on salam in meat with resolution and related rulings on meat as qimi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding salam in meat, explain the basis of each position, and identify the mufta bihi view with its tarjih authority.

Core Idea
Salam in meat is valid when fully specified — fatwa follows Sahibayn despite Abu Hanifa's objection.

This passage examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: whether salam (advance payment for deferred delivery) is valid for meat. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states it is not valid, following Abu Hanifa. However, his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), permit it if the meat is fully described. Later Hanafi authorities resolved the conflict by adopting the Sahibayn's view as the operative fatwa, provided the specification eliminates uncertainty. The passage also addresses the legal classification of meat as a qimi (value-based) item, contrasting it with bread (mithli) in matters of guarantee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling in the Matn and Its Attribution
Locate the phrase 'ولا يصح السلم في اللحم' and note that the commentator immediately qualifies it as Abu Hanifa's view. Understand that the matn's bald statement is not the final school position.
This is a classic example where the matn reflects one imam's view, but the school's fatwa may differ.
2
State the Sahibayn's Position and Their Dalil
The Sahibayn permit salam in meat if 'جنسه ونوعه وسنه وموضعه وصفته وقدره' are specified. Their proof: meat is a weighed item that can be precisely described, analogous to tail fat (ألية) and fat (شحم).
Analogy (qiyas) to accepted salam items.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's Objection and Its Two Bases
Abu Hanifa argues that meat varies due to bone size (كبر العظم وصغره) and seasonal fatness (الفصول سمناً وهزالاً), leading to potential dispute. Two narrations from him on boneless meat reflect this.
The dispute is not about the principle of salam but about the sufficiency of description.
4
Examine the Resolution: Conditioned Specification
The text notes that the disagreement is resolved by conditioning: Abu Hanifa's prohibition applies when salam is absolute (مطلقاً), while the Sahibayn's permission applies when fully specified. This is the view adopted for fatwa.
This resolution harmonizes the positions and is cited from al-Bazaziyya.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi and Its Authority
The commentator explicitly states 'وفي الحقائق والعيون: الفتوى على قولهما' — fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view. This is the relied-upon position in later Hanafi practice.
Tarjih authority: later works like al-Haqa'iq, al-'Uyun, and al-Bazaziyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا يصح السلم في اللحم أي عند أبي حنيفة وقالا يجوز إذا بين جنسه ونوعه وسنة وموضعه وصفته وقدره كشاة خصي ثني سمين من الجنب أو الفخذ مائة رطل لأنه موزون مضبوط الوصف فصار كالألية والشحم بخلاف لحم الطيور فإنه لا يقدر على وصف موضع منه وله أن يختلف باختلاف كبر العظم وصغره فيؤدي إلى المنازعة. وفي منزوع العظم روايتان والأصح عدمه ولذا أطلقه في الكتاب. وفي الحقائق والعيون: الفتوى على قولهما. قوله: (وله أنه يختلف باختلاف كبر العظم وصغره قال في الفتح: وعلى هذا الوجه يجوز السلم في مخلوع العظم وهو رواية الحسن عنه، ثم ذكر للإمام وجهاً آخر وهو أنه يختلف بحسب الفصول سمناً وهزالاً قال : وحاصل هذا الوجه أنه سلم في المنقطع وعلى هذا لا يجوز في مخلوع العظم وهو رواية أبي شجاع عنه . قال المصنف : وهو الأصح .اهـ. قوله : (إلى وسط المنتقى) الذي في الفتح وسط غصب المنتقى . قوله : ويشترط أن يكون المكيال بما لا ينقبض الخ) كذا في الهداية قال في النهر قال الشارح : وهذا لا يستقيم في السلم إلا إذا كان لا يعرف قدره فلا يجوز السلم به. وقد قيل لا خلاف فمنع أبي حنيفة فيما إذا أطلقا السلم في اللحم، وقولهما فيما إذا بينا وإذا حكم الحاكم بجوازه صح اتفاقاً؛ كذا في البزازية واللحم قيمي فيضمن بالقيمة إذا غصب كما في الجامع الكبير من باب الاستحقاق وعزاه في الصغرى إلى وسط المنتقى وفي فروق الكرابيسي: يضمن اللحم عند الإتلاف بالقيمة والخبز يضمن بالمثل، ولو اشترى باللحم يثبت ديناً في الذمة والخبز كذلك، فالحاصل أن اللحم مع الخبز يستويان في ثبوتهما ديناً في الذمة ويفترقان في الضمان فيضمن اللحم بالقيمة والخبز بالمثل. والفرق أن كل واحد منهما وإن كان غذاء لكن الخبز أبين غذاء وأحسن كفاً فأظهرنا حكم التفرقة في الضمان والتسوية في الدينية عملاً بالشبهين اهـ. التتمة وفي اختيار شيخ الإسلام على الأسبيجابي أن اللحم مضمون بالمثل. وفي الظهيرية: وإقراض اللحم عندهما يجوز كما يجوز السلم وعن أبي حنيفة روايتان واللحم مضمون بالقيمة في ضمان العدوان إذا كان مطبوخاً بالإجماع، وإن كان نيأ فكذلك وهو الصحيح. وإن اشترى شيئاً بلحم في الذمة ذكر في الإجارات أنه إذا استأجر شيئاً بلحم في الذمة جاز وما يصلح أجرة في الإجارة يصلح ثمناً في البيع اهـ.
He said: ('and salam in meat is not valid') i.e., according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Sahibayn) said it is permissible if its genus, type, age, place, description, and quantity are specified, like a castrated ram, a thani, fat, from the side or thigh, one hundred ratls, because it is a weighed item with a specifiable description, so it becomes like the tail fat and fat. Unlike bird meat, because it is not possible to describe a specific part from it, and it can differ based on the size of bones, leading to dispute. Regarding boneless meat, there are two narrations, and the more correct is its impermissibility, hence the author left it general. In al-Haqa'iq and al-'Uyun: the fatwa is on their (the two's) view. He said: ('and he has that it differs according to the size of bones') al-Fath said: On this basis, salam in deboned meat is permissible, which is a narration from al-Hasan (from Abu Hanifa). Then he mentioned another basis for the Imam: it differs according to seasons, fatness and leanness. He said: the net of this basis is that it is salam in a discontinued item, and on this it is not permissible in deboned meat, which is a narration from Abu Shuja' from him. The author said: this is the more correct. He said: ('to the middle of al-Muntaqa') what is in al-Fath is 'middle of Ghasp al-Muntaqa'. He said: It is a condition that the measure be something that does not expand or contract, etc. Thus in al-Hidaya; in al-Nahr, the commentator said: This is not valid in salam unless its capacity is not known, so salam by it is not permissible. And it has been said there is no disagreement; Abu Hanifa's prohibition is when they make salam in meat absolutely (without specification), and their (the two's) permissibility is when they specify. If a judge rules its permissibility, it is valid by agreement. Thus in al-Bazzaziyya. Meat is a qimi (value) item, so it is guaranteed by value if usurped, as in al-Jami' al-Kabir from the chapter of istihqaq. In al-Sughra, it is attributed to the middle of al-Muntaqa. In Furuq al-Karabisi: Meat is guaranteed by value when destroyed, and bread is guaranteed by the like. If one buys with meat, it becomes a debt in the dhimmah, and similarly bread. So the conclusion is that meat and bread are equal in being established as a debt in the dhimmah, but differ in guarantee: meat is by value, bread by the like. The difference is that both are nourishment, but bread is a clearer nourishment and better in form, so we manifest the ruling of difference in guarantee and equality in being a debt, acting on both similarities. The supplement: In Ikhtiyar of Shaykh al-Islam on al-Asbijabi, that meat is guaranteed by the like. In al-Zahiriyya: Lending meat is permissible according to the two (Sahibayn), just as salam is permissible, and from Abu Hanifa there are two narrations. Meat is guaranteed by value in tortious guarantee if cooked by consensus, and if raw, it is likewise, and this is the correct view. And if one buys something with meat in the dhimmah, it is mentioned in al-Ijarat that if one rents something with meat in the dhimmah, it is permissible, and what is valid as a rental fee is valid as a price in sale.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage addresses the controversial issue of salam in meat. The matn states it is not valid, which is the position of Abu Hanifa. However, his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn), permit it provided the meat is thoroughly specified: genus, type, age, body part, and weight. The commentator explains that Abu Hanifa's objection is that meat varies due to bone size and seasonal fatness, leading to potential dispute. For boneless meat, there are conflicting narrations from Abu Hanifa; the preferred view is its impermissibility. A later resolution is cited: the disagreement is not fundamental; Abu Hanifa's prohibition applies to absolute salam without specification, while the Sahibayn permit it with full specification. If a judge rules its permissibility, it is valid by agreement. The passage then discusses the legal treatment of meat as a qimi (value-based) item, contrasting it with bread (mithli). Meat is guaranteed by value when destroyed, while bread is guaranteed by the like. However, both can be established as debts in the dhimmah. The text also touches on lending meat and using meat as a price in sales and rentals, indicating that meat can function as a deferred payment (in salam) according to the Sahibayn, but with differences in guarantee.

Key Terms
لحم قيمي (lahm qimi): Meat is considered a value-based (qimi) item, not a mithli, so it is guaranteed by value rather than by the like.
السلم (al-salam): A sale where the price is paid upfront and the goods are delivered later; a contract of advance payment.
مطلق (mutlaq): Absolute or unconditional; in this context, salam without specification of the meat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position regarding salam in meat in the Hanafi school according to the text?
A) It is absolutely invalid.
B) It is valid only for boneless meat.
C) It is valid if specified in detail as per Sahibayn.
D) It is valid only for cooked meat.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits salam in meat if fully specified, and meat is treated as a qimi (value-based) item in guarantee.

Salam with Unknown Measure or Non-Rigid Container
Ruling on salam with unknown or non-rigid measure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid measure in salam and identify which types of containers render the contract invalid.

Core Idea
A sale is invalid if the measure is unknown or the container can expand—certainty in delivery is required.

In salam (advance payment sale), the quantity must be known precisely. The Hanafi school requires the measuring tool to be rigid and known. This lesson explores the ruling when the measure or its capacity is unknown, and the exception made by Abu Yusuf for water skins due to customary practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on unknown measure
The text states salam is invalid if the measure (mikyal or dhira') is not known in capacity because it leads to potential loss and dispute.
2
Understand the reason
The possibility of loss (diya') creates uncertainty (gharar), which invalidates the contract.
Relates to the prohibition of gharar fahish.
3
Contrast with cash sale
If sold immediately (cash), an unknown measure is allowed because the buyer sees the goods directly, removing uncertainty.
Cash sale vs salam: different risk profiles.
4
Note the required type of measure
The measure must not contract or expand; bowls (qisa') are valid, but bags (jirab) and baskets (zanbil) are not.
Flexible containers introduce uncertainty.
5
Analyze Abu Yusuf's ruling on water skins
He allowed salam in water using water skins (qirbah) due to customary practice, but conditions apply (e.g., must be a known measure and customarily accepted).
An exception based on 'urf (custom).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وبمكيال أو ذراع لم يدر قدره) أي لا يصح لاحتمال الضياع فيقع النزاع بخلاف البيع به حالاً قيد بكونه لم يدر قدره لأنهما لو كانا معلومي القدر جاز، ويشترط أن يكون المكيال مما لا ينقبض ولا ينبسط كالقصاع وأما الجراب والزنبيل فلا يجوز الكيل بهما . وعن أبي يوسف الجواز بقرب الماء للتعامل وهو سقاء كذا وكذا قربة من أن يشتري من النيل أو غير ذلك مثلاً بهذه القرية وعينها جاز البيع وتقتضي القاعدة المذكورة أن لا يجوز إذا عين هذه القرية ولكن بمقدارها ؛ كذا في فتح القدير وفي القنية : السلم في الماء مختلف فيه؛ فإن كان موضعاً جرت العادة فيه بالسلم وذكر الشرائط صح اه قوله : (وبر قرية أو تمر نخلة معينة) أي لا يجوز لاحتمال أن يعتريهما أفة فلا يقدر على التسليم وإليه أشار بقوله «أرأيت إذا منع الله ثمرة هذا البستان يستحل أحدكم مال أخيه؟ فإن معناه أنه لا يستحق بهذا البيع شيئاً إن لم يخرج ذلك البستان شيئاً فكان في بيع ثمرة هذا البستان غرر الإنفساخ يصح بخلاف ما إذا أسلم في حنطة صعيدية أو شامية فإن احتمال أن لا ينبت في الإقليم شيء برمته ضعيف فلا يبلغ الغرر المانع في الصحة، ولذا قيد بالقرية احترازاً على الإقليم وتعيين البستان كتعيين النخلة . هذا لو كانت نسبة الثمرة إلى قرية معينة لبيان الصفة لا لتعيين فلا بم.
He said: ('and with a measure or cubit whose capacity is not known') meaning it is not valid because of the possibility of loss, leading to dispute, unlike selling with it immediately (cash). It is conditioned that it is not known because if both are known in capacity, it is permissible. It is a condition that the measure be something that does not contract or expand, like bowls (qisa'). As for the bag (jirab) and basket (zanbil), measuring with them is not permissible. From Abu Yusuf: permissibility of water in water skins (qirbah) due to customary practice. It is a waterskin; so-and-so waterskin: if one buys from the Nile or similar, for example with this waterskin and it is specified, the sale is valid. The mentioned principle requires that it is not permissible if this specific waterskin is specified but only as its measure; thus in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Qunyah: salam in water is disputed; if it is a place where salam is customary and the conditions are mentioned, it is valid. He said: ('and with the crop of a specific village or dates of a specific palm tree') meaning it is not valid because of the possibility that they may be affected by blight, so he cannot deliver. And he indicated this by his saying: 'Do you see that if Allah prevents the fruit of this garden, will any of you consider his brother's wealth lawful?' Its meaning is that he does not deserve anything from this sale if that garden does not produce anything. So in the sale of fruit of this specific garden, there is gharar (uncertainty) leading to dissolution. It is not valid, unlike if one makes salam in Egyptian or Syrian wheat, because the probability of an entire region not yielding anything is weak, so the uncertainty does not prevent validity. Hence he restricted it to a specific village to avoid the region. Specifying the garden is like specifying the palm tree. This applies if the attribution of the fruit to a specific village is for description, not for specification, then it is not...
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage covers two related rulings on invalid salam due to uncertainty. First, salam is invalid if the measure (mikyal) or cubit (dhira') used is unknown in capacity, because it leads to potential loss and dispute. However, if the exact capacity is known, it is valid. The measure must be rigid (non-expanding/contracting) like bowls; flexible containers like bags or baskets are not allowed. A specific ruling on water in waterskins: Abu Yusuf allowed it due to custom, but careful conditions apply. Second, salam in the crop of a specific village or dates of a specific palm tree is invalid because of the risk of blight (natural disaster) rendering delivery impossible. The commentator cites a hadith: 'Do you see that if Allah prevents the fruit of this garden, will any of you consider his brother's wealth lawful?' This indicates that such a contract involves excessive uncertainty (gharar). In contrast, salam in regional wheat (e.g., from Egypt or Syria) is valid because the chance of total failure across the whole region is negligible. The key is whether the specification is for description (na't) or for designation (ta'yin); if it is for description, it is permissible; if for designation, it is not.

Key Terms
الغرر (al-gharar): Uncertainty or risk that renders a contract invalid, such as tying delivery to a specific source that may fail.
المكيال (al-mikyāl): A measuring instrument for volume, such as a container or cup.
الجراب (al-jirāb): A bag made of cloth used for storing or measuring, considered invalid for measuring in salam due to its flexibility.
الزنبيل (al-zanbīl): A basket woven from reeds, used for carrying goods, but invalid for measuring in salam due to its inconsistency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a valid measure for salam?
A) A known cubit (dhira')
B) A bowl (qasa')
C) A cloth bag (jirab)
D) A rigid container

Key Takeaway
For a valid salam, the measuring tool must be rigid and its capacity known; flexible containers are invalid.

Salam in the Crop of a Specific Village or Dates of a Specific Tree
Ruling on salam with specific village or tree

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why salam tied to a single risky source is invalid and distinguish between designation (ta'yin) and description (na't).

Core Idea
Salam in a specific village's crop or a single tree's fruit is invalid due to risk of blight—only general description is allowed.

The second part of the passage addresses salam where the commodity is tied to a single source, such as a specific village's wheat or a particular palm tree's dates. The risk of blight (āfah) or failure makes delivery uncertain, rendering the contract invalid. A hadith is cited to illustrate the injustice. However, if the attribution is merely descriptive (e.g., 'Egyptian wheat'), it is valid because regional failure is rare.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited specifications
Salam in the crop of a specific village (bar qaryah) or dates of a specific palm tree (tamr nakhla mu'ayyana) is invalid.
2
Understand the reason
Possibility of blight (āfah) preventing delivery creates excessive uncertainty (gharar fahish).
3
Analyze the prophetic wisdom
The hadith 'Do you see if Allah prevents the fruit of this garden, will any of you consider his brother's wealth lawful?' shows the contract would be unjust.
The hadith is cited as evidence of gharar.
4
Distinguish from regional description
Salam in 'Egyptian wheat' is valid because the risk of complete regional failure is negligible; uncertainty does not reach the level of prohibition.
The threshold is 'weak probability' of total loss.
5
Differentiate between description (na't) and designation (ta'yin)
The prohibition applies only when the source is designated for delivery. If the attribution is for quality description only, it is permissible.
Example: 'dates from Madinah' as description is valid; 'dates from this specific tree' is not.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Salam in Location-Specific Goods and New Crops
Ruling with proof on salam in location-specific goods and new crops

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on salam in location-attributed goods and new crops, distinguishing valid from invalid cases based on custom and the possibility of cessation.

Core Idea
Salam is invalid if the commodity may cease to exist before delivery; attribution to a location is judged by custom—quality indication permits it, place specification does not.

Salam (advance payment sale) is a concession for mutual benefit, but it carries risk. This passage explores two critical issues: when goods are associated with a location (e.g., Herati wheat vs. Herati cloth) and when they are brand new crops. The Hanafi school uses custom ('urf) and the possibility of the commodity becoming unavailable (inqita') to determine validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that this is a salam contract. The ruling (sahih or fasid) depends on whether the commodity is likely to exist from contract to delivery.
2
Apply the custom (urf) test for location attribution
Determine whether the attribution to a place indicates a specific origin (which risks cessation) or merely a quality/style. If custom treats it as quality, it is valid; if as place, invalid.
The passage contrasts Herati wheat (invalid) with Herati cloth (valid).
3
Consider temporal existence for new crops
For new crops, check whether the crop exists at the time of the contract. If the crop has not yet appeared, salam is invalid due to potential unavailability. If it already exists, it is valid.
This applies to wheat, corn, wool, milk, etc.
4
Distinguish between essential and manufactured goods
Note that for manufactured goods like cloth, the attribution is to a type or style, not a specific production site, so the risk of cessation is minimal. For agricultural produce, the risk is higher.
The text uses wheat vs. cloth as an example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخارج من أرضها بعينه كالحشراتي ببخارى والسباخي وهي قرية حنطتها جيدة بفرغانة لا بأس به لأنه لا يراد خصوص النابت هناك بل الإقليم، ولا يتوهم انقطاع طعام إقليم بكماله فالسلم فيه وفي طعام العراق والشام سواء كذا في ديارنا قمح الصعيد. وفي الخلاصة وغيرها: لو أسلم في حنطة الهراة لا يجوز، وفي ثوب هراة وذكر شروط السلم يجوز لأن حنطتها يتوهم انقطاعها إذا لإضافة لتخصيص البقعة فيحصل السلم في موهوم الانقطاع بخلاف إضافة الثوب لأنها لبيان الجنس والنوع لا لتخصيص المكان، وكذا لو أتى المسلم إليه بثوب هروي نسج في غير ولاية هراة من جنس الهروي يعني من صفته ومؤنته يجبر رب السلم على قبوله فظهر أن المانع والمقتضى العرف فإن تعورف كون النسبة لبيان الصفة فقط جاز وإلا فلا؛ كذا في فتح القدير ثم قال وفي شرح الطحاوي لو أسلم في حنطة حديثة قبل حدوثها فالسلم باطل لأنها منقطعة في الحال وكونها موجودة في وقت العقد إلى وقت المحل شرط اهـ. وفي الجوهرة ولو أسلم في حنطة جيدة أو في ذرة جديدة لم يجز لأنه لا يدري أيكون في تلك السنة شيء أم لا .اهـ. وعلى هذا فما يكتب في وثيقة السلم جديد عامه مفسد له ولكنه ينبغي حمله على ما إذا كان قبل وجود الجديد أما بعد وجوده فيصح كما يشير إليه ما في شرح الطحاوي وفي الخلاصة: وكذا إذا أسلم على صوف غنم بعينها أو ألبانها وسمونها قبل حدوثها أو سمن حديث لأنه لا يُدْرِى بقاؤه.
As for (crops from) its specific land, like al-Hashrati in Bukhara and al-Sabakhi—a village whose wheat is good in Farghana—there is no harm, because what is intended is not the specific produce of that place but the region, and there is no fear of the complete cessation of a region's food. So salam in it and in the food of Iraq and Syria is the same, as in our lands: wheat of al-Sa'id. In al-Khulasa and others: If one pays salam in wheat of Herat, it is not permissible; but in a cloth of Herat, mentioning the conditions of salam, it is permissible, because the wheat may be feared to cease, since the attribution is for specifying the place, so salam occurs in something whose cessation is possible, unlike attribution of cloth because it is for indicating the genus and type, not for specifying the place. Similarly, if the seller brings a Herati cloth woven outside the province of Herat but of the Herati type—meaning its description and quality—the buyer must accept it. Thus it becomes clear that the preventing factor and the requirement are custom: if custom is that the attribution indicates the description only, it is permissible; otherwise no. As in Fath al-Qadir. Then he said: In Sharh al-Tahawi: If one pays salam in new wheat before its occurrence, the salam is invalid because it is unavailable at present, and its existence from the time of contract to the time of delivery is a condition. End. In al-Jawhara: If one pays salam in fine wheat or new corn, it is not permissible, because one does not know whether anything of it will exist that year. End. Based on this, what is written in the salam document as 'new of its year' invalidates it, but it should be interpreted as referring to before the new crop exists; after it exists, it is valid, as indicated in Sharh al-Tahawi. And in al-Khulasa: Similarly, if one pays salam in the wool of specific sheep, or their milk and fat, before their occurrence, or new ghee, because one does not know its continuance.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and reasoning concerning salam (advance payment) in goods that are location-specific or newly produced. The Hanafi school holds that salam is valid only if the commodity is likely to exist from the time of contract to the time of delivery. For location-specific produce like wheat from Herat, the attribution indicates a particular field, so there is risk of total crop failure; thus salam is invalid. In contrast, for cloth from Herat, the attribution indicates a style or quality, not a specific place, so there is no such risk—the cloth can be produced elsewhere with the same description. Custom (urf) determines the interpretation: if custom treats the location as a quality indicator, it is valid. The same reasoning applies to new crops: salam before the crop exists is invalid due to potential unavailability; after it exists, it is valid. The passage also covers similar cases for wool, milk, and ghee from specific animals before they are produced.

Key Terms
السلم (al-salam): A sale where the price is paid in advance and the commodity is delivered later, a concession to address the needs of the poor.
الانقطاع (al-inqita'): The possibility that the commodity becomes unavailable, making salam invalid.
العرف (al-'urf): Custom that determines whether attribution to a location indicates quality or specific place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is salam in 'wheat of Herat' invalid but 'cloth of Herat' valid?
A) Because wheat is a staple food and cloth is not
B) Because the attribution for wheat specifies a particular place whose produce may cease, while for cloth it indicates a type/quality
C) Because the Hanafi school prohibits salam in all agricultural products
D) Because cloth can be imported from elsewhere but wheat cannot

Key Takeaway
The validity of salam in location-attributed goods depends on custom: if the attribution signals quality, it is valid; if it signals a specific place, it risks invalidity due to possible cessation.

Conditions for Salam and the Measure Issue
Conditions for salam and the compressible container issue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five conditions for a valid salam contract and explain why a compressible container (munkabis) invalidates the specification of quantity.

Core Idea
In salam, quantity must be precisely fixed; a compressible container creates uncertainty and invalidates the contract.

The salam contract allows advance payment for deferred delivery of specified goods. To prevent disputes, the Hanafi school requires clear specification of genus, type, quality, quantity, and delivery term. This lesson explores these conditions, with special attention to the requirement of precise measurement and why a compressible container fails to meet it.

Guided Path
1
List the five conditions for salam
From the source text, identify the five required specifications: genus (jins), type (naw'), quality (sifa), quantity (qadr), and delivery term (ajal).
These conditions eliminate ignorance (jahala) about the subject matter.
2
Understand the dual application of the first four conditions
The first four specifications apply to both the capital (price) and the commodity, making eight specifications in total. This ensures that both parties know exactly what is being exchanged.
The term is only required for the deferred commodity, not the immediate capital.
3
Examine the requirement of precise quantity
Quantity must be known exactly; uncertainty (gharar) invalidates the contract. The text discusses salam in a vessel (qirba) whose capacity is known but may compress or expand.
The Hanafi position is that such vessels are not permissible because they lead to potential dispute.
4
Analyze the compressible container case
If the container compresses (yanqabid) or expands (yanbasit), the exact quantity at delivery is uncertain, causing potential conflict. The contract is therefore invalid.
This is based on al-Hidayah and affirmed by later commentators.
5
Evaluate the counter-argument and the Hanafi resolution
Some argue that if the quantity can be known after measuring, there is no dispute. The Hanafi response is that the container itself cannot be determined by a specific measure, so uncertainty remains.
Al-Nahr clarifies that the condition of precise quantity is not about knowledge after the fact, but about inherent specifiability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وشرط) بيان الجنس والنوع والصفة والقدر والأجل كقوله حنطة سقية جيدة عشرة إكرار إلى شهر لأن الجهالة تنتفي بذكر هذه الأشياء فهذه خمسة الأربعة الأول منها تشترط في كل من رأس المال والمسلم فيه فهي ثمانية بالتفصيل، فإن ما يجوز كونه مسلماً فيه كيفما كان وإن كان يعرف قدره فالتقدير به لبيان القدر لا لتعيينه فكيف يتأتى فيه الفرق بين المنكبس وغيره والتجويز في قرب الماء، وإنما يستقيم هذا في البيع إذا كان يجب تسليمه في الحال حيث يجوز بإناء لا يعرف قدره ويشترط في ذلك الإناء أن لا ينكبس ولا ينبسط ويفيد فيه استثناء قرب الماء اهـ. وعلى ما في الهداية جرى الحدادي ولم يتعقبه في فتح القدير بل أقره، وهذا لأنه إذا أسلم في مقدار هذا الوعاء براً وقد عرف أنه دويبة مثلاً جاز غير أنه إذا كان ينقبض وينبسط لا يجوز لأنه يؤدي إلى النزاع وقت التسليم في الكبس وعدمه. وقول الشارح إنه لا يتعين ممنوع، نعم هلاكه بعد العلم بمقداره لا يفسد العقد ولم أر من أوضح هذا فتدبره. والله تعالى الموفق اهـ . كلام النهر: قلت: منع عدم تعينه غير ظاهر وأي نزاع بعد معرفة مقداره ويمكن العدول إلى ما عرف من مقداره فيسلمه به بلا منازعة كما إذا هلك، وقد ظهر لي في الجواب عن الهداية أن ما ينقبض وينكبس بالكبس لا يتقدر بمقدار معين فتبقى المنازعة وعليه فيكون قوله واشترط الخ لبيان المراد من قوله "لم يدر قدره لا أنه شيء زائد عليه تأمل
His saying: (and condition is) the specification of genus, type, quality, quantity, and term, like saying: wheat, irrigated, good, ten ikrar, until a month, because ignorance is removed by mentioning these things. So these are five; the first four are required in both the capital and the commodity, so they are eight in detail. For what is permissible as the commodity, even if its capacity is known, then measuring by it is to indicate the quantity, not to specify it. So how can the difference between something that compresses and something else and the allowance of a water skin be achieved? This is only correct in a sale where delivery must be immediate, where it is permissible with a container whose capacity is not known, but that container is conditioned to neither compress nor expand, and the exception of a water skin is useful therein. End. Based on al-Hidayah, al-Hadadi followed it, and Fath al-Qadir did not criticize but affirmed it. This is because if one pays salam in the measure of this vessel for wheat, and it is known that it is, for example, a certain insect, it is permissible. However, if it compresses and expands, it is not permissible because it leads to dispute at the time of delivery regarding compression or not. The commentator's statement that it is not specific is refuted. Yes, its destruction after knowing its quantity does not invalidate the contract, and I have not seen anyone who clarified this, so reflect. And Allah is the granter of success. End. The speech of al-Nahr: I say: The prevention of its non-specificity is not apparent, and what dispute is there after knowing its quantity? It is possible to turn to what is known of its quantity and deliver it accordingly without dispute, as if it had perished. And it has become clear to me in answer to al-Hidayah that what compresses and expands with compression cannot be determined by a specific measure, so dispute remains. Therefore, his saying "and he stipulated" etc. is to explain the intended meaning of his saying "he does not know its quantity," not that it is something extra over that. Reflect.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a definition and expansion of the conditions for a valid salam contract. It identifies five essential specifications: genus, type, quality, quantity, and the delivery term. The first four apply to both the capital (price) and the commodity, making eight specifications in total. The text then delves into a key point: when the quantity is measured by a container whose capacity might vary (like a vessel that can compress or expand), it leads to uncertainty and potential disputes. Following al-Hidayah, such a container is not permissible for salam because it fails to establish a precise quantity. The commentary by al-Nahr refines this, noting that if the actual quantity can be known (e.g., after measuring), the contract remains valid, but the inherent ambiguity of a compressible container is problematic. Thus, the condition of precise quantity is crucial: the commodity must be clearly quantifiable to avoid future conflict.

Key Terms
المكيل (al-makil): Good measured by volume, like grains; one of the categories in which salam is valid.
المنكبس (al-munkabis): Something that can be compressed, leading to variation in volume when measured.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, why is a compressible container (ينقبض وينبسط) not valid for specifying quantity in a salam contract?
A) Because the container may be destroyed after measuring
B) Because it leads to potential dispute at delivery over the actual quantity
C) Because the container must be made of animal skin
D) Because such containers are not used for measuring grain

Key Takeaway
A valid salam requires precise specification of all five elements, and any uncertainty in quantity, such as using a compressible container, invalidates the contract.

Additional Conditions for Salam: Capital, Place, Option, and More
Lists additional conditions for a valid salam contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and explain the additional conditions (10th–18th) required for a valid salam contract in Hanafi fiqh, and apply them to real contractual scenarios.

Core Idea
Salam requires strict additional conditions to eliminate uncertainty and avoid riba.

The basic five conditions of salam (genus, type, quality, quantity, term) are not enough. Hanafi jurists identified at least nine more conditions to ensure the contract is free from gharar (uncertainty) and riba. These conditions regulate the capital, the commodity, the place of delivery, and prohibit options. Understanding these will help you distinguish valid salam contracts from invalid ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the additional conditions
From the passage, list the conditions starting from the tenth: (10) specification of the term, (11) place of delivery for heavy goods, (12) receipt of capital before separation, (13) avoidance of riba causes in both counterparts, (14) no option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart), (15) specific identification of commodity (not naqdayn), (16) existence of commodity from contract to delivery, (17) commodity from measurable categories (makiul, mawzun, madhru', ma'dud), (18) specification of capital quantity for fungible goods (mithliyyat).
The passage also mentions earlier conditions from al-Iydah regarding adding a term after contract if capital still exists.
2
Categorize conditions by focus area
Group them: Capital-related (receipt, scrutiny, quantity specification), Commodity-related (existence, specific identification, measurable categories), Contractual (no option, no riba cause, place of delivery, term specification).
Categorization aids memorization and understanding of each condition's purpose.
3
Understand the rationale behind each condition
For example, prohibiting khiyar al-shart eliminates uncertainty in delivery; requiring receipt of capital before separation ensures trust and prevents riba; specifying place of delivery for heavy goods avoids disputes about where the commodity must be delivered.
The underlying theme is avoiding gharar and riba, as salam is a concession for urgent need.
